Eve of the Naval Conference Opening; Comparison of the Policies of Five Countries; British Naval Chief of Staff Meets with Japanese Representatives

(London) The British Chief of Naval Staff, Admiral Chatfield, recently met at the Admiralty with the Japanese representative to the naval conference, Admiral Nagano, and former Japanese Ambassador to Germany, Nagai, as well as Iwashita Terazaki, a member of the Japanese delegation. British naval expert Sir Herbert Richmond and the Director of the American Department of the Foreign Office, Craigie, were also present. It is reported that the British and Japanese representatives discussed the procedural issues of the naval conference. These procedural issues will also be discussed by Naval Minister Monsell when he meets with the representatives of the United States, France, and Italy tomorrow afternoon. Furthermore, the French delegation held a meeting at the French Embassy this morning, chaired by the French Ambassador to the UK, Goulin, who is also the chief representative to the conference. The current situation was discussed at the meeting. (Havas Dispatch on the 7th)

(London) With the London Naval Conference about to open, representatives from various countries have arrived one after another. The following is a summary of the positions of the United Kingdom, Japan, the United States, France, and Italy, as ascertained by our reporters.

(1) The United Kingdom's position is based on setting qualitative restrictions for various classes of warships. However, if the countries cannot agree on the figures proposed by the United Kingdom, they can be modified. (A) Regarding the tonnage of various classes of warships, the British Admiralty proposes that the tonnage of battleships be limited to 25,000 tons, but if necessary, it can be revised to a maximum tonnage of 35,000 tons, as suggested by the United States. The tonnage of cruisers should be limited to 7,000 tons, aircraft carriers to 22,000 tons, and destroyers to 1,500 tons. At the same time, it also advocates the complete abolition of submarines. (B) Regarding the caliber of guns for various classes of warships, the United Kingdom proposes that the caliber of battleship guns be limited to 12 inches, and cruisers to 6 inches.

(2) Japan advocates abolishing capital ships or substantially reducing the number and tonnage of capital ships. In addition, it advocates abolishing 10,000-ton class cruisers and reducing the tonnage of cruisers, because Japan considers both capital ships and 10,000-ton class cruisers to be offensive weapons. As for submarine fleets, Japan believes they are defensive weapons and insists on retaining them.

(3) The United States, in contrast to Japan's position, strongly desires to maintain its capital ship and big gun doctrine, which it has always upheld. It argues that the minimum tonnage for battleships should be 35,000 tons and does not seem to insist much on the tonnage of cruisers, but if it is limited to 7,000 tons, it will definitely not accept it. As for Japan's demand for equality, it cannot be accepted by the United States.

(4) Although France and Italy are both prepared to accept the agreement on restrictions, they are unwilling to abandon the two 35,000-ton battleships they are currently building. Both countries also advocate maintaining submarines. It is also reported that the Italian delegation is now trying to avoid disputes with France. As for the neutralization of the Mediterranean Sea and the Strait of Gibraltar, they do not intend to make demands. In addition, the French Admiralty, considering the country's relatively long overseas colonial transportation lines, argues that the country's naval power should exceed that of any other continental European country. Furthermore, since the Anglo-German naval agreement was concluded, Germany's naval power will follow British naval policy and increase accordingly (35 percent). As a result, France's naval power will also increase accordingly, and Germany will also definitely follow France's shipbuilding policy, even for 35,000-ton battleships. This is because of the Anglo-German naval agreement, and it is the difficulty facing the naval conference. (Havas Dispatch on the 7th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government has decided on its countermeasures for the disarmament conference. It will first decide on the method of arms reduction, based on the qualitative restrictions agreed upon and other related issues. It then instructed the resident British representatives to advocate at the conference that the principle of disarmament should be discussed first. According to a report from Fujii, the acting ambassador to the UK, the conference will establish a committee of plenipotentiaries from various countries to seek a breakthrough in reaching a principled understanding. Therefore, it is still doubtful whether the UK and the United States will agree. It is also possible that Japan and the UK and the United States will start discussions on qualitative issues at the beginning of the conference. (Japan United Press Dispatch on the 7th)

(Washington) Official sources here have remained silent regarding the statement made by the spokesperson of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs that Japan intends to abandon the Nine-Power Treaty relating to China. However, private sources are expressing considerable doubt about Japan's statement. The official unwillingness to comment is due to the fact that the Japanese spokesperson was speaking in a personal capacity and said that Japan does not wish to take any action on this matter at present. Responsible parties believe that this statement is a probe or a diplomatic tactic for the naval conference. (National News Agency Dispatch on the 6th)

(London) After arriving here, the U.S. delegation to the Naval Conference had dinner at their hotel last night. They do not intend to meet with any naval representatives from the UK or other countries before the opening of the Naval Conference. Its chief delegate, Norman Davis, also does not intend to issue any statements on the upcoming discussions before the formal conference. The delegation currently believes that the conference will be lengthy. According to observations by Americans here, the outcome of the Naval Conference is not very optimistic, as there are two major obstacles ahead. One is that the current general situation is sufficient to have an adverse impact on the progress of the conference, and the other is that there is no unanimous agreement among the countries concerned on the principle of the tonnage ratio of major naval powers, which will inevitably hinder the establishment of a naval agreement. (Havas Dispatch on the 7th)

(London) Admiral Bini, Rear Admiral Piccia, and experts from the Italian delegation to the Naval Conference arrived here at 5:20 p.m. this afternoon. Rear Admiral de Gueux, Colonel Deporcain, Captain Berger, and experts from the French delegation also arrived on the same train as the Italian representatives. (Havas Dispatch on the 6th)

(London) The London Naval Conference is scheduled to open within days. According to the observations of a Havas reporter, the biggest obstacle facing the Naval Conference is the conflict between the views of the United States and Japan. If the Japanese representatives insist on naval equality as a prerequisite for discussing all issues, it is feared that the Naval Conference will immediately reach a stalemate after it opens. As for the UK, it will probably try to reconcile and propose to discuss various specific technical issues first, so that the Naval Conference can proceed in an orderly manner without wasting time. However, no matter how hard the UK tries, the main issues caused by the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty will inevitably be raised at the Naval Conference sooner or later. It is expected that the discussion will involve the political aspects of the Pacific region, as the United States wants to build new military bases on the main transportation routes in the Far East, while Japan will definitely oppose it. Therefore, the Naval Conference will inevitably discuss the balance of power in the Far East. (Havas Dispatch on the 6th)

British and American Joint Venture for Transatlantic Air Route; Five-Nation Conference Decides, But Must Wait Two Years

(Washington) Representatives from the United Kingdom, the United States, Southern Ireland, Canada, and Newfoundland met at the State Department here today and agreed to launch a transatlantic air route plan as soon as possible. United Airlines and British Imperial Airways will jointly operate the service. It is generally believed that this service is unlikely to be realized within a year, and the opening date is still two years away. The routes currently under discussion are one northern route, traveling between New York, Montreal, Botwood, and Ireland, and one southern route, traveling between New York, Bermuda, and the Azores. The northern route is the most popular. (Reuters Dispatch on the 6th)

Alameda, California – The China Clipper landed here at 10:36 this morning, completing its round-trip Pacific Ocean flight. The aircraft circled San Francisco Bay once before landing on the water near Alameda. The journey from San Francisco took a total of 17 hours. Around 5,000 local residents gathered at the airport to welcome it. The airline announced that the entire round trip took 123 hours. (6th National Telegram)

Alameda – The China Clipper arrived here today, thus concluding the first round trip of the flying boat between California and Manila across the Pacific. The round trip took a total of 123 hours and 13 minutes. The return flight from Manila to California took 63 hours and 28 minutes. The final leg, from Honolulu to California, covered 2,410 miles and took 17 hours, with an average speed of 140 miles per hour. (6th Reuters)

Abyssinian Emperor Protests Italian Aircraft Bombings - League of Nations to Implement Oil Embargo Early - Italian Aircraft Bomb Taisi for Second Time - Previous Bombing Caused Hundreds of Casualties

(Geneva) It is rumored here that the Italian aircraft bombing of Taisi will accelerate the League of Nations' oil embargo against Italy. It is expected that the 48-nation committee meeting next week will be brief and the resolution to adopt the oil embargo will receive unanimous support. The implementation of the oil embargo will not be delayed much. (7th Reuters)

(Geneva) According to sources in the League of Nations, the kerosene embargo will be announced before the New Year. Therefore, political activities regarding the Italian-Abyssinian conflict will soon be intensified. Sir Drummond, the British Ambassador to Italy, met with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini this morning to gauge Mussolini's intentions so that British Foreign Secretary Hoare could ascertain Italy's political stance before meeting with French Prime Minister Laval in the afternoon. He also advised Mussolini to use moderate language when addressing the Chamber of Deputies. In addition, Mr. Vasconcelos, Chairman of the Eighteen-Nation Committee, told reporters that Hoare and Laval were likely to discuss the implementation date of the kerosene embargo at their meeting today. Ottawa – Canadian Prime Minister King announced today that his government's statement on the oil embargo refers to its origin and does not involve its merits. Canada's attitude towards the League of Nations has not changed. Canada will still support the League of Nations if it imposes an oil embargo and implements other sanctions, but the phrase "Canadian motion" will no longer be used. (7th National Telegram)

(Geneva) The Abyssinian Emperor sent a personal telegram to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol, strongly protesting against the Italian aircraft bombing of undefended towns, villages, and hospitals. He stated that representatives of major British and American newspapers could prove the bombing of the American hospital in Taisi, and he personally witnessed the tragic death of a woman and two children. The hospital suffered significant damage and prominently displayed the Red Cross flag, which Italian aircraft should have been able to see. (7th Reuters)

Taisi – An Associated Press reporter's investigation today revealed that 53 people were killed and 200 injured in the Italian bombing of this place. Many of the injured suffered from missing limbs. Doctors were busy amputating broken limbs. One of the injured was a Swiss nurse, whose leg had been amputated. In addition, dozens of women and children were injured. Italian aircraft did not attack the Abyssinian army stationed in the suburbs, which strengthens the belief that the Italian aircraft's target was the Abyssinian Emperor. (6th Guomin News Agency Telegram)

Addis Ababa – The people of Addis Ababa were greatly angered after hearing the news of the Italian aircraft bombing of the undefended town of Taisi yesterday. At the same time, they were overjoyed that the Abyssinian Emperor had escaped unharmed. It is reported that the Emperor had ordered the city to be equipped with anti-aircraft guns for defense. Italian aircraft attacked three times yesterday, with a total of nine aircraft dropping approximately 1,000 incendiary and explosive bombs. Thirty-two people were killed and 200 injured. The Emperor personally aimed and fired at the enemy aircraft. The Emperor was standing in his imperial garden at the time, and although bombs exploded near him, he remained calm. One bomb exploded less than fifteen feet away, injuring several soldiers, but the Emperor was unharmed. The American hospital that was hit was run by an American church. One Norwegian nurse was injured and had a leg broken. The people in the hospital had evacuated a few minutes before the enemy aircraft appeared. The hospital's office was destroyed, and beds, surgical instruments, surgical tables, and other equipment were scattered all over the ground. There was also other damage. Rumors circulated that one enemy aircraft had been shot down, but this could not be confirmed. Many people in Addis Ababa feel that the war has truly begun. At the same time, according to unconfirmed reports, fierce fighting is taking place in Duolo, near Magaal. (7th Reuters)

(New York) News received here from Addis Ababa states that Italian aircraft attacked the town of Taisi yesterday, and a bomb hit a hospital run by an American church, injuring one American nurse. The hospital was completely destroyed, and medicines and equipment were scattered in all directions, making it extremely difficult to treat the wounded. Abyssinian people, whose homes were destroyed, cursed the white people indiscriminately, apparently not distinguishing between Italians and other foreigners. (7th Reuters)

Addis Ababa – It was officially announced here today that fierce fighting had taken place fifteen miles south of Duolo, with heavy losses on both sides. Today, Italian forces bombed Gondar for the second time, killing four women and two children. The troops under General Aliyu and General Imanu were attacked by bombs and machine guns. Italian aircraft also attacked Meking Gao and Ositelosa. Italian military aircraft flew over Harar and Angor, but did not drop bombs, although it is predicted that Jijjiga, Harar, and Addis Ababa will eventually be attacked. It is reported that Italian forces are currently advancing on Taikazi. (6th Guomin News Agency Telegram)

Addis Ababa – Italian aircraft bombed the town of Taisi again today. Details are unknown. It is reported that Gonda, a key city in northwestern Abyssinia, was also bombed by Italian aircraft, killing four women and four children and injuring another twenty people. Italian aircraft dropped a total of 178 bombs. According to an official report signed by seven doctors at the American hospital in Taisi, when twelve Italian aircraft attacked Taisi yesterday, the American hospital was their primary target, and bombs rained down. At the same time, former commander-in-chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, General De Bono, stated in the Roman Gazette today that Italian reconnaissance aircraft had flown over tens of thousands of armed Abyssinian camps near Taisi. Although Italian aircraft were heavily bombarded by Abyssinian anti-aircraft guns, they bombed the enemy camps with great effect. (7th Reuters)

(London) The Chronicle reported that one of the bombs dropped by Italian aircraft landed less than fifteen feet away from Abyssinian soldiers, and these Abyssinian soldiers were only six feet away from the Emperor. The Emperor then returned fire with anti-aircraft guns. As soon as he heard the sound of a bomber, he rushed to the anti-aircraft gun to fire. Soldiers tried to cover the Emperor's shoulders with a cloth to avoid making him a target, but the Emperor ignored them and continued to open fire next to Michael. (7th Guomin News Agency Telegram)

Four Spies Attempt Theft - French Military Mobilization Plan - Guard Opens Fire, Repelling Them

(Paris) Today, four people attempted to break into a safe at the Bourget Airport to steal the French mobilization plan. They were spotted by a guard, who opened fire. The four people fled without a trace. (7th National Telegram)

1,500 Kilometers Apart - Indirect Negotiations Between Britain, France, and Italy - Hoare and Laval Meet in Paris - Mussolini Addresses the Chamber of Deputies - Prospects for Italian-Abyssinian Peace Improve Again

(Paris) The Foreign Ministers of Britain, France, and Italy held talks today. However, the Italian Foreign Minister, Prime Minister Mussolini, was 1,500 kilometers away from the British and French Foreign Ministers. This form of long-distance indirect talks is unprecedented in diplomatic history. This morning, British Foreign Secretary Hoare arrived here and agreed to meet with Prime Minister Laval in the afternoon, after Prime Minister Mussolini's broadcast address in Rome concluded. This allowed Hoare and Laval to fully understand the content of Mussolini's speech before their meeting. Mussolini met with British Ambassador to Italy, Sir Drummond, this morning to discuss matters. The so-called triangular British-French-Italian diplomatic talks were thus realized. According to what this newspaper's correspondent has learned, the diplomatic talks between Britain, France, and Italy, which began today, are in a better situation than the gloomy outlook generally expected in recent days. Italy had previously stated that it would refuse mediation efforts by Britain and France, and had threatened that while Italy could consider suggestions from other countries, it would not make any new suggestions itself. At that time, diplomatic circles and Italian public opinion spread alarming news that a European war was about to break out. Now, it seems that Britain and France are no longer insisting that Italy automatically make new suggestions, so the situation has become more moderate, and the Italian government's firm attitude is not as severe as previously imagined, which is somewhat satisfactory. (7th Havas)

(Paris) Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval is scheduled to meet with British Foreign Secretary Hoare at 5:30 PM. According to what this newspaper's diplomatic correspondent has learned, Italian Ambassador Cerruti reiterated the seriousness of the kerosene embargo to Laval this morning. The French Foreign Ministry believes that the kerosene embargo can only be delayed if Italy changes its attitude and strives for peace. However, according to what this newspaper's correspondent has learned, Hoare and Laval believe that Italy's intentions are extremely difficult to grasp, so the joint British-French plan to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute may be decided at a later date. (7th Havas)

(London) When British Foreign Secretary Hoare meets with French Prime Minister Laval in Paris today, British Under-Secretary Vansittart will also be present. He has arrived in Paris. Before leaving London yesterday, he had talks with the French and Italian Ambassadors. It is reported that although British and French experts have not yet completed their peace proposals, they will report the results of their discussions to Hoare and Laval tomorrow. It is now hoped that the two officials will be able to agree on a concrete plan to submit to Italy and Abyssinia. At present, there is no indication that the Italian government is prepared to start negotiations on terms that the British and French governments would consider appropriate. (7th Reuters)

(Rome) Mussolini decided to address the Chamber of Deputies at 3:00 PM today, and it will be translated into 17 languages and broadcast worldwide. The Italian people are now waiting for the Prime Minister to announce his attitude towards the Abyssinian war and the League of Nations' sanctions. It is reported that the content of Mussolini's speech will be both firm and moderate. (7th National Telegram)

Italian Chamber of Deputies Autumn Session Opens - Mussolini Speaks - Says Overall Situation Slightly Improved

(Rome) The Chamber of Deputies held its autumn session this afternoon. When Mussolini attended the opening ceremony, he spoke and ridiculed France's participation in the sanctions against Italy. Before the opening, the entire chamber sang patriotic songs. At 2:00 PM, Mussolini entered the chamber, and everyone stood up and cheered. More than 400 deputies attended, all wearing black uniforms. Only the 43 deputies serving in East Africa were absent. Mussolini spoke about the sanctions, saying that the overall situation has now improved slightly. The proposed sanctions may be slightly relaxed, but deputies should not be too optimistic. The Italian government was previously asked to state its immutable needs, and it notified the French government of this in October. Unexpectedly, the countries did not offer suggestions but retaliated with sanctions. Mussolini then referred to the talks between British and French experts in Paris, saying that there was no reason to believe that they would reach a quick resolution. Then, Speaker Count Ciano announced the opening of the meeting and said that all Italian people were determined to resist unfair sanctions, so they were now contributing all their gold to the country. The deputies were also willing to hand over all their gold medals. Ciano then drew the deputies' attention to the fact that Mussolini had handed over all his medals except the one he won for the "March on Rome." Mussolini also handed over his steel helmet to be reforged into pure steel. Then, the deputies walked to the ballot box and put their medals into a box. The French and American Ambassadors were seated in the diplomatic gallery, but the British Ambassador was not seen. Hours before the opening, the public gallery was already full. (7th Reuters)

(Rome) The Italian Chamber of Deputies held a meeting this afternoon. Prime Minister Mussolini entered the chamber at 3:00 PM, and all the deputies, dressed in black shirts, applauded and cheered for the Prime Minister. Slogans were written all over the podium, listing the names of the countries participating in the sanctions. Mussolini then delivered a speech, stating that the international situation was unlikely to improve. The Italian people should not be overly optimistic. As for the British and French experts who are holding talks in Paris, they are not formal negotiations. Mussolini then reiterated his opposition to sanctions and said that British Foreign Secretary Hoare's speech in the House of Commons, which said that "Britain deeply wishes Italy to have a strong and capable government," was ironic, as Italy had been working hard for fourteen years to create a strong and capable government. The final conclusion of the Italian Prime Minister's speech was: "I hereby solemnly declare that unless Italy's rights are recognized and Italy's interests in Africa are guaranteed, there can be no true right or wrong. Italy, on the one hand, is justified and, on the other hand, must continue to act in Italy and Africa. The Italian army and the Blackshirts, on expedition in Africa, will undoubtedly win victory for the motherland." (7th Havas)

Artistic Musings

The Face of a Clock (Part 2)

— Feng Zikai

People living in the present era probably look at the face of a clock more often than they look at the faces of their superiors, bosses, friends, or lovers. Students, teachers, workers, shop assistants, people in post offices, people in train stations… who doesn't look at the face of a clock several times a day? Even those who live secluded lives, enjoying comfort and luxury, those of noble birth and wealth, who have others attend to their every need, cannot help but constantly observe the expression on the clock's face. It is a reasonable request to hope that the appearance of this face, which is constantly seen by so many eyes every day, becomes more pleasing. I remember when we first saw it, its face was marked with delicate Roman numerals. The many radiating lines created a sense of both pattern and numerical significance. Although intricate, it was gentle and refined, with a distinctly antique style. I can't recall in which century it was born in the West, but I know that Matteo Ricci brought it to China during the Wanli reign of the Ming Dynasty (late 16th century). So, I assume it was a product of the 16th century or earlier. Roman numerals were probably its original appearance? Because the delicate radiating lines and elegant patterned style remind me of the artistic forms of the Renaissance and the court art era. About thirty years ago, when we were children, its face was still marked with Roman numerals; later, it suddenly transformed, and all clocks, large and small, had Arabic numerals inscribed on their faces. I don't know when this trend started, or in which country or by whom it was created, as I am not a scholar of arts and crafts. But one can imagine that this is a manifestation of the "utilitarianism" of the late 19th century, an expression of "intellectualism" in arts and crafts. Because using 12345, etc., with rectangles as the basic form and strokes of varying complexity, to adorn the circumference of a circle, and making each one face me, though there are conveniences in terms of practicality and intellectual perception, the form inevitably suffers from a sense of "awkwardness." Especially the rectangular watches that are popular among women now: because of the forced attempt to fit the four sides of a rectangle to the circular motion of the hands, the size and spacing of the Arabic numerals become uneven, resulting in an awkward expression. Now that I think about it, when I disliked the faces of clocks and painted them over, though it was an act of curiosity, it was probably also partly due to their awkward expressions.

The clock with Arabic numerals has been showing its awkward face to the world for several decades now. There must be sensitive artists and craftsmen who dislike it, hence the emergence of the Art Nouveau style clock. "Simple and clear" is the aesthetic form demanded by modern sensibility. Furniture with carved dragons and phoenixes has now been replaced by glass tables and steel tube chairs. Sumptuous palaces have now been replaced by glass houses, skyscrapers, and steamboat-style buildings. All kinds of arts and crafts have followed this trend towards "simplicity and clarity," and this clock can be said to be one of its pioneers. Speaking of its advantages, first: clocks have been in use for a long time, and we are very familiar with the parts of its face. Therefore, using only a line to indicate the hour, without numerals, is beneficial to the form without hindering practicality. Second: using a line to indicate the hour, because of its small footprint and uniformity, the distance between every five minutes is very clear, much clearer than Roman numerals, much clearer than Arabic numerals. We can see the minutes correctly at a glance. Third: the hands are free of decorative patterns (the hands of old-fashioned clocks were curved on both sides, with a circle at the tip, and sometimes a ruyi-shaped tassel was attached below the circle), its indication is direct, swift, frank, and clear, unlike the rambling of old-fashioned hands. —In these three points, I praise the face of the new clock. But I cannot determine that this is the most reasonable form of clock in terms of overall progress; I just think it looks better than one with Arabic numerals. I also cannot determine that this face can please everyone; I just feel that at least it can provide comfort to the vision of some people. I said "everyone," which is really too careless! In the interior of our country, in the vast and remote countryside, there are still countless people who have never seen the face of a clock! Night of December 3rd

Song Zheyuan Goes to Tangshan for Rest; Japanese Planes Fly Over Beiping for Reconnaissance for Days

Beiping Dispatch: The situation in North China, since He Yingqin arrived in Beiping, has been discussed in detail with the Beiping-Tianjin authorities every day. Song Zheyuan, due to the mental fatigue of dealing with the situation in recent months, went to the Xiyuan at 11:00 AM on the 5th from his private residence in Wuyiku Hutong to inspect Feng Zhian's troops. At 1:00 PM, he went to Tangshan for rest and had not returned as of the 6th. Before leaving, he issued a written statement stating, "The precarious and turbulent situation in North China, since Minister He came to Beiping to coordinate the overall plan, there is hope for a turn for the better. Moreover, Minister He has met with Chairman Han (Fuju) and Chairman Shang (Zhen), and has a genuine understanding of the actual situation in North China, so a complete solution can naturally be obtained. From now on, all difficult problems should be handled under the responsibility of Minister He."

Regarding the issue of stabilizing the situation in North China, internal contacts have been emphasized in recent days. Chen Yi and Xiong Shihui, who accompanied He Yingqin to Beiping, only had a private meeting with a certain important Japanese figure in Beiping once. Formal contacts have not yet begun. In order to quickly centralize internal opinions, He summoned Chen, Xiong, Qin Dechun, Xiao Zhenying, and others again at Jurren Hall at noon on the 5th for a meeting, the result of which was satisfactory. He will remain in Beiping temporarily to handle everything. A certain important Japanese figure once expressed to a certain individual, roughly stating that they do not intend to insist on preconceived notions regarding the North China issue, but recently there has been a change in attitude, roughly stating that the solution should not deviate far from the spirit of their proposed plan. Therefore, the focus of discussion among all parties in recent days has been on this point. Song Zheyuan, because his personal responsibility has been reduced since He Yingqin came north, and at the same time, the Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Headquarters has received orders from the central government to prepare for dissolution, hopes to end it as soon as possible. On the 5th, he sent Qin Su to see He to express this intention politely. A Japanese reconnaissance plane, all silver-gray, without a number, carrying a Japanese officer, flew from Chengde via Tongzhou to Nanyuan at 12:20 PM on the 5th and landed. At that time, another Japanese reconnaissance plane flew from the Dongjuzi Japanese airfield in Tianjin and circled over the city of Beiping for about ten minutes. Then, three more Japanese reconnaissance planes flew from Tianjin, and after another ten minutes, five more Japanese planes arrived. At 1:50 PM, nine Japanese planes gathered over the city of Beiping, divided into three rows, each with three planes, circled and flew over the central area of the city for about twenty minutes, and flew back to Tianjin at about 3:00 PM. Also, Japanese plane No. 23, piloted by a Japanese named Yuta, carrying a person in civilian clothes, flew from Tianjin to Nanyuan at 3:20 PM on the afternoon of the 10th. The Japanese are building a new airfield near Liminzhuang near Dongjuzi in Tianjin, which has been actively built by the Japanese army with aviation troops. All work was completed on the 5th. The airfield occupies more than 1,300 mu of land and can accommodate 30 aircraft. Kubota, the chief of staff of the Japanese Lushun Naval Base, is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin on the 7th to set up a Tianjin office. Tianjin Issues Copper Coin Notes

Temporarily Issued by the Provincial Bank as a Circulating Fund The Construction Department Asks Officials to Stabilize Prices

Tianjin Dispatch: The issuance of Tianjin copper coin notes was realized on the 5th. According to central government orders, the issuance of copper coin notes does not require additional preparations and has been assigned to the Beiping Agricultural and Industrial Bank under the Finance Department. The order has arrived in Tianjin, but the Beiping Agricultural and Industrial Bank is hesitant and watching due to the time required for preparation and the current precarious situation in Hebei. However, Tianjin, due to the absorption and manipulation of various unscrupulous merchants in the concessions, has a sluggish market circulation, and the people's livelihood is becoming increasingly strained. If issuance is not expedited, unexpected riots may occur. Therefore, the City Chamber of Commerce, the Nine Districts Construction Office, and the Silver and Money Industry Association jointly discussed and decided to telegraph Chairman Shang Zhen of the Hebei Provincial Government, ordering the Hebei Provincial Bank to provide temporary assistance by issuing old copper coin notes to facilitate market circulation. Shang replied by telegram on the 3rd, approving the request, but with two conditions: (1) It is a temporary arrangement, and the copper coin notes will be withdrawn after the bank designated by the Finance Department issues copper coin notes. (2) Before issuing the old copper coins notes stored by the Hebei Provincial Bank, a legal price (i.e., exchange rate) should be set to avoid confusion and losses for the people when exchanging them. At 10:00 AM on the 4th, City Police Chief Liu Yushu, City Chamber of Commerce Chairman Ji Hua, Banking Association Chairman Zhong E, Money Industry Association Chairman Wang Xiaoyan, Hebei Provincial Bank Deputy Manager Wang Zocai, Tzu Lian Hui President Zhao Pinqing, and representatives of the exchange industry held a joint meeting to decide on five measures: (1) The use of Hebei Provincial copper coin notes will begin on December 5th. (2) The price of copper coins is temporarily set at 460 coins to exchange for one yuan of legal tender. (3) Regardless of whether it is copper coin notes or copper coins, holding 460 coins can be exchanged for one yuan of legal tender at the Hebei Provincial Bank. (4) All merchants dealing in copper coins must calculate the price of goods sold in either copper coin notes or copper coins according to the rate of 460 coins to one yuan of legal tender and must not arbitrarily increase prices. (5) The tram company will accept all copper coin notes, but passengers holding copper coins must still purchase tickets with copper coins. After the meeting, the Public Security Bureau telegraphed the City Government with the meeting's details and issued a notice to the public on the 5th. Regarding the amount of issuance, according to Hebei Provincial Bank Deputy Manager Wang Zocai, the bank, upon receiving Chairman Shang's telegram order and local requests, is issuing the existing copper coin notes as a temporary emergency measure. The amount issued this time is approximately 200,000 yuan, with denominations of ten coins, twenty coins, forty coins, sixty coins, and one hundred coins, partly unused notes that have already been printed and partly intact notes that have been issued and recovered. Because the market urgently needs them, it was originally planned to issue them on the afternoon of the 4th, but the procedures could not be completed in time, so it was changed to the morning of the 5th. Copper coins are also very scarce in Baoding, and they plan to issue copper coin notes recently. These copper coin notes can be circulated in the cities of Beiping and Tianjin and within the territory of Hebei Province, etc. The City Nine Districts Construction Office believes that although the copper coin panic has passed, the prices of various commodities have indeed increased significantly. On the 4th, they gathered at the First District Construction Office to discuss and earnestly request the authorities to quickly stabilize prices to maintain the people's livelihood. (5th)

Songjiang: Two Guns Recovered in Robbery Case

In the case of the robbery of the Lianyun automobile on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway in Yangjia Temple, Punan Eighth District, the Provincial Department severely ordered the county government to arrest the perpetrators, with severe punishment for any violations. After the 12th Detachment Headquarters and the Water Patrol Team jointly captured the bandits Zhang Xiaobao, Gen Gou, and Little Monk, they were sent to Songjiang for interrogation and then transferred to the local court for questioning. On the 6th, Water Patrol Team Captain Fei Gongxia, based on confidential reports that the bandit leader Li had secretly returned to Shuike, led Patrol Officer Yu and Lieutenant Adjutant Wang Wenxiong of the 12th Detachment Headquarters to patrol Shuike. They vaguely saw figures and shouted for the password, but there was no response. They fired three shots as a warning, and the figures scattered and fled. They tracked them in the dim night, but there was no trace. Searching along the path, they found two Jiu Yu rifles and one empty cartridge case hidden in the rice straw in the cemetery. One of the rifles was missing its firing pin. They continued to search until dawn and returned to the team headquarters, then transferred the guns to the county government. The gun numbers are 1409 and 324. It is said that these guns were the weapons robbed from the Xiahengjing Watch Post in Majing Township, Seventh District. They were used to rob and loot Zhujiaxing.

Suzhou: Detention of Merchants and Citizens Causes Panic in Various Industries

Zhu Dongmei butcher shop on Pingjiang Road in Suzhou City sent its employee Zhang Heshang to Changzhou to purchase goods a few days ago. While passing Pingdoukou, the police found 300 double-dime silver coins on Zhang Heshang, suspected of smuggling, and took him to the Public Security Bureau for detention. Later, with the approval of the county government by the County Chamber of Commerce, Zhang was temporarily released on bail on the afternoon of the 6th. The county government submitted the large number of silver dimes to the province for instructions. However, the 30-odd trade associations in Wu County, including fresh meat, rice, oil, wine, sauce, southern goods, silk, wood, and woolen goods, were alarmed by the incident, fearing that the small change used in trade was inevitable. Moreover, the market continues to operate as usual, but income cannot be exported, and all industries will come to a complete standstill. During the winter season, the need for silver dimes to pay grain taxes and settle accounts is urgent. Banks are not ubiquitous in villages and towns, and the villagers are at a loss. If silver dimes cannot be taken from one county to another, and the Beijing-Shanghai trains pass more than a dozen times a day, and they are bound to be tired of searching, how can travelers be spared harassment? It is found that silver dimes are commonly known as subsidiary currency, and the Finance Department's telegram explained that silver refers to real silver and miscellaneous silver, which proves that silver dimes are not included in the restrictions, nor is there a prescribed quantity or restriction on use within the territory. This time, since the employee has proven to be a legitimate merchant, the Public Security Bureau has inevitably implicated innocent people and seems to have abused its power. On the afternoon of the 7th, they jointly telegraphed the County Chamber of Commerce to submit it to the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting that they issue a clear order to correct the situation and reassure businesses.

Wuxi: Police Mobilize to Inspect Tent Households

The Wuxi County Public Security Bureau, in view of the current winter defense period and the fact that petty thieves are taking the opportunity to commit thefts and robberies are occurring frequently in urban and rural areas, and that tent households and awning boats easily harbor bandits, has formulated a tent household inspection plan and secretly ordered each sub-bureau and directly subordinate sub-stations in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, and sixth districts to conduct a full mobilization on the 6th and 7th to carry out inspections. A total of more than 450 officials, officers, and police officers participated, departing simultaneously at 5:00 AM, while paying attention to household registration and doorplates at all times. The results of the inspection showed that the total number of tent households was: 928 in the first sub-bureau, 554 in the second sub-bureau, 1,302 in the third sub-bureau, 2,045 in the fourth sub-bureau, 791 in the fifth sub-bureau, 1,559 in the sixth sub-bureau, and 1,112 in the first sub-station, totaling 8,291. At the same time, the county water patrol team also conducted a thorough inspection of the awning boats in the territory and monitored the movement of those passing through at all times. During the inspection, the Hongqiao Wang Zhaofu thatched tent in the first sub-bureau and the Gu Futai thatched tent in Changjie Mushatou in the third sub-bureau were found to contain opium paste and smoking paraphernalia. Also, in the Xu Yulin tent household in Xishuiguan in the first sub-bureau, 83 silver dollars, 18 paper dollars, 12.3 dimes, 19,000 copper coins, a silver necklace weighing 3 liang and 6.2 qian, two silver bracelets weighing 3 liang, and a silver chain weighing 1 liang were found. As there was so much cash in the thatched tent, the circumstances were suspicious, and they were all taken to the bureau for transfer to the county for interrogation.

Yangzhou: Representatives of the Daily Newspaper Association Petition

Regarding the case of the dispute over the arrest of a reporter from the Zhonghua Daily by the Security Police Team of the County Public Security Bureau, the Daily Newspaper Association convened a meeting on the 6th and selected 16 representatives who went to the County Party Headquarters and the County Government at 10:00 AM on the 6th with petitions. County Executive Committee Member Yu and County Magistrate Ma of the County Government received them in person, adopted the representatives' statements, accepted the petitions, and expressed satisfaction. The representatives then took their leave and departed.

Education Broadcast Supplement

Our Country's Scientific Research Undertakings (Continued)

(Speech to secondary school students nationwide on November 26th)

Ding Wenjiang, Director-General of the Academia Sinica (Speech to secondary school students nationwide on November 26th)

Today, I want to talk about the liaison and cooperation in scientific undertakings in our country. But first, I want to explain the history and mission of the Academia Sinica.

The Academia Sinica was established in April of the 17th year of the Republic [1928]. According to its organizational law, it is the highest academic research institution of the Republic of China, directly under the National Government. Its mission is twofold: first, to carry out scientific research, and second, to guide, liaise with, and encourage academic research. To carry out the first type of mission, the Academia Sinica has established a total of ten research institutes. The three institutes of physics, chemistry, and engineering are located in Shanghai because they need to liaise with industrial institutions at home and abroad. In addition, the general organs of astronomy, meteorology, geology, botany and zoology, psychology, history and language, social sciences, and management administration are all concentrated in Nanjing. From this, it can be seen that the scope of research of the Academia Sinica is extremely broad, encompassing most of the natural sciences on the one hand, and social sciences and history and language on the other. To understand the content of its research, we can analyze its tasks into three types.

The first is a number of routine tasks, such as the astronomical observatory's calculation of almanacs, observation of variable stars, and counting sunspots daily; the meteorological observatory's observation of temperature, air pressure, and wind direction, and reporting of weather, which clearly belong to this category. Not only that, but ordinary chemical analysis, standard engineering tests, physical geomagnetic measurements, geological mapping, and collection of botanical and zoological specimens can all be considered a kind of routine task. Strictly speaking, this cannot be considered research, but it is the basis of many research works, and often takes a long time to achieve results. For example, engineers need to build bridges and prevent floods, and agricultural and forestry experts need to improve production and promote forests, all of which require knowing the average rainfall in these areas for many years. In any country, this kind of work is undertaken by the government, and the institutions that undertake this task are often independent. In China, however, it is accidentally accommodated under a single general organ—the Academia Sinica. This, of course, can have obvious advantages, because under one organ, it is relatively easy for those who do this work to communicate with each other, help each other, and unify and cooperate all work, so as to accomplish the most tasks with the least amount of funding.

The most important and practical task of the Academia Sinica is to use scientific methods to study our country's raw materials and production. In our industrially backward country, it is very difficult to have new and different inventions of our own. However, we have our own special natural products and traditional skills. If we can understand the quality of our raw materials and the principles of production, it will be easy to use new methods to improve old industries or develop new resources. For example, in terms of minerals, using geological methods to discover new mines, I mentioned the achievements of the Geological Survey of the Ministry of Industry in my last speech. Now I want to give an example of the achievements of the Geological Institute of the Academia Sinica.

Fushanpu in Pingyang, Zhejiang, has always been a place where alum is produced. Five years ago, Mr. Ye Liangfu, a researcher at the Academia Sinica, went to investigate and found out that this is the largest alunite mine in the world. Its reserves are nearly 300 million tons. Alunite is originally a kind of potassium aluminum sulfate. We now use indigenous methods to make it into alum, which is of little value and has a very narrow market. The annual output is worth only more than 600,000 yuan. If we can process the original alunite into alumina on the one hand, as a raw material for aluminum smelting; and on the other hand, process it into potassium sulfate, or use a part of the sulfuric acid to manufacture ammonium sulfate; the result will be that alum, which has very limited uses, will be transformed into several kinds of essential products with extremely large markets. The annual production capacity can definitely be increased several times. Currently, the Institute of Chemistry of the Academia Sinica and the Chemical Industry Society in Tanggu are both working on this issue. Because there are still technical difficulties, it has not yet reached the stage of real success. But knowing that the reserves of Fushanpu's alunite mine are so large is the starting point of this research. Because alunite mines are of course also available in foreign countries, but the reserves are relatively small, so they are not worth paying attention to, and it is not worth studying new methods to use them to manufacture aluminum or fertilizers. Since we know that this kind of alunite mine is a very large resource for us, of course we are not willing to let it go easily, and only use it as a raw material for manufacturing alum.

Everyone knows that porcelain was invented by our ancestors. In recent years, our porcelain industry has slowly declined and cannot compete with Japanese porcelain. The most important reasons are nothing more than two: first, the workers who manufacture porcelain only know how to follow the methods passed down from previous generations to make blanks, glazes, and fire kilns. Regarding all functions, they only know the what but not the why. For example, why is it that the same clay with the same appearance can be used to make white porcelain in Jingdezhen, but can only be used to make purple clay in Yixing? If you ask a porcelain-firing worker, he cannot tell you the reason. Therefore, not only can it not be improved, but also because of changes in the quality of raw materials, the products deteriorate. Second, because foreign porcelain is made by machines, the quality has certain standards. We are completely handmade, and the quality cannot be consistent. If you go to a porcelain shop to see the bowls produced in Jiangxi, the size and shape of the products from the same kiln are not the same, you will know the advantages and disadvantages of the new and old industries, and the path we should strive for. The Academia Sinica has established a ceramic testing ground in the Institute of Engineering. First, it cooperates with the Geological Institute to thoroughly study the geological genesis and reserves of clay and glaze materials from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, and Hunan, and use standard methods to collect mineral samples for analysis and testing, so that various raw materials can be standardized. (Standardization) Then select the raw materials with the richest reserves and the most suitable mineral quality, and use small-scale machinery to test and manufacture pottery. This work has not started for long, but I believe that there will be considerable results in the short term, which can serve as the basis for the revival of our pottery industry.

There are also many methods commonly used in agriculture and industry that may be possible in foreign countries but not in China. If you want to imitate others, you must understand the Chinese environment and re-study it yourself. For example, cotton has several important diseases and pests, such as anthracnose, angular leaf spot, seedling blight, and damping-off. These are all because bacteria harm cotton seeds. Some of these bacteria live on the shell of the cotton seeds, and some are hidden in the soil. In foreign countries, when sowing, the cotton seeds are disinfected with medicine on the one hand, and poison is sprinkled in the soil on the other hand. In China, these methods cannot be adopted. First, because medicines have to be purchased from foreign countries, the price is too expensive, and second, because our farmers are too poor to afford this disinfection capital. And these diseases and pests are extremely prevalent in our country. Cotton that has suffered from these diseases either turns black and spotted or withers, causing great losses every year. Recently, Mr. Deng Shuqun of the Institute of Botany and Zoology of the Academia Sinica has studied this problem and found a solution. According to his experiments, if the cotton seeds are soaked in boiling water before sowing, the toxic bacteria attached to the cotton seed shell can be killed. The cotton seed shell is very thick, and soaking it in boiling water is not only harmless but can also make it germinate earlier. Then apply mercuric chloride and grass ash to the cotton seeds and then sow them, and the above-mentioned diseases can be completely eliminated. Mercuric chloride is a kind of poison that can kill bacteria in the soil. Because it is not sprinkled in the soil but mixed with grass ash, the bactericidal effect is the same and the amount required is less. Moreover, it is the habit of our country's farmers to mix seeds with grass ash before sowing, so this method does not require much labor. Boiling water does not cost much money. According to Mr. Deng's calculation, using his method, each mu of land only needs to use one tael of mercuric chloride to be effective. One tael of mercuric chloride costs only a little more than one jiao at market price, which is much more economical than the old method used in foreign countries. If our farmers can use this method to grow cotton, each mu only needs to spend a very small amount of money to completely prevent four diseases and pests, and the reduced losses will be at least ten times more than the money spent on disinfection.

Ephedra was originally an old Chinese medicine, but the method of use was extremely unscientific. Since Mr. Chen Kehui's research at Peking Union Medical College proved that the ephedrine contained in ephedra is a specific medicine for treating asthma, the true effect of ephedra has become clear. Therefore, the Beiping Research Institute has specially set up a Drug Research Institute, inviting Mr. Zhao Shimin to study Chinese medicinal materials, and the Institute of Chemistry of the Academia Sinica also has people cooperating with Mr. Zhao to do this work. But more important than drugs is our food problem. Everyone knows that the efficiency of Chinese laborers is extremely low, less than half of that of Europeans and Americans. For example, Chinese miners work twelve hours a day and can only mine an average of half a ton of coal. British miners, under almost the same circumstances, work eight hours and can mine 1.2 tons of coal. However, during the European War, these Chinese miners were transported to France by the British to dig trenches. Eating bread and beef, the work efficiency was no less than that of Western Europeans. The same is true for working-class workers and petty-bourgeois students. Anyone who has examined the bodies of Chinese students knows that the physical development of Chinese students is generally not healthy. The reason is because the food they eat is not nutritious enough. We cannot hope that everyone can eat meat, but we hope that those who study chemistry will study our usual foods, determine their nutritional value, so that we can use a scientific basis to redistribute our food. According to the research of Professor [missing character] Ben of Tsinghua University, the vitality contained in Beiping's [missing character] is the same as that of American oranges. Although this is the case, not only should poor people eat more [missing character], but rich people can also buy less American oranges. The Institute of Chemistry of the Academia Sinica is working on this kind of problem. If we can improve our food within the scope of our country's national economic capacity, the working efficiency of the general public will definitely increase a lot.

The Ministry of Communications Orders Shipping Companies to Comply with Silver Transportation Regulations

The Ministry of Finance Has Formulated Six Regulations; Severe Punishment Will Be Meted Out for Any Smuggling

The Ministry of Communications has issued a special order to all state-owned and private shipping bureaus to comply with the six regulations on the transportation of silver coins and silver categories, which have been formulated by the Ministry of Finance. The regulations are as follows: (Article 1) The transportation of silver coins and silver categories shall be carried out by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. The aforementioned banks transporting silver coins and silver categories shall hold a transportation passport approved by the Ministry of Finance in order to be transported. Customs checkpoints or military police along the way shall verify the passport and release the goods. (Article 2) In places where the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications do not have branches or agencies, silver coins and silver categories exchanged by banks, money shops, pawnshops, post offices, railways, ships, telegraph bureaus, national and local tax collection agencies, county governments, and other public agencies or public organizations shall be immediately sent to the nearest Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, or their agencies, to exchange for legal tender. When transporting, the exchange agencies shall also prepare a certificate stating the number of silver coins or silver categories and the name of the bank exchanging for legal tender for verification by the military police along the way, and notify the nearest bank exchanging legal tender to facilitate liaison. However, when notifying customs checkpoints, the passport issued by the Ministry of Finance shall be verified for release. (Article 3) Those who purchase silver materials in accordance with the Silver Product Management Rules shall be given a certificate by the bank selling the silver materials for verification. However, when passing through customs checkpoints, the passport issued by the Ministry of Finance shall be verified for release. (Article 4) Anyone who transports silver coins or silver categories privately without a passport or a certificate from the exchange agency shall be confiscated and turned over to the government by the military police, government agencies, or customs. If it is found that the silver categories seized in the aforementioned item have been deliberately concealed with the intention of smuggling and evading export, the offenders shall be sent to the local court for punishment in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on the Punishment of Offenses Against the National Currency. (Article 5) Within the time limit for exchanging legal tender, people in all places may carry silver coins or silver categories to the nearest exchange agency to exchange for legal tender. (Article 6) Except for those stipulated in Articles 1, 2, 3, and 5, travelers going abroad or traveling domestically, as well as those in boats and vehicles, are not allowed to transport or carry silver coins or silver categories. Violators shall be handled separately in accordance with the provisions of Article 4.

Brief Biography of Mr. Gosh, the U.S. Consul General in Shanghai; However, There Is No Definite Date for His Arrival in Shanghai

The Continental News reports that the U.S. Department of State has recently appointed Gosh, a first-class diplomatic affairs officer, as the U.S. Consul General in Shanghai. The exact date of his arrival in Shanghai is currently unknown, and he will probably not arrive in Shanghai to take office until a few months later. Gosh was born in Washington in 1887. He joined the Department of State in 1903. He came to Shanghai in 1907 as acting Consul General, and returned to Washington in 1909. In 1912, he was reappointed as acting Consul General in Shanghai. In 1915, he was appointed as Deputy Consul in Shanghai. Later, he served as Consul General in Tianjin, Xiamen, Jinan, and Fengtian. In 1924, he resumed his position in Tianjin. After two years, Kenningham asked for leave to return to the United States, so he came to Shanghai to temporarily take over the position of Consul General, and then returned to Tianjin. In 1931, he was transferred back to the Department of State in Washington. In 1933, he was appointed as Consul General in Paris and Counselor of the U.S. Embassy. He is still stationed in Paris. Before Gosh takes office, the position of Consul General in Shanghai is still being managed by Davis, who has recently been promoted to first-class diplomatic affairs officer.

Ministry of Finance's Reply to the Chamber of Commerce: Remembering Measures to Stabilize Sichuan Exchange Rates

After the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to stabilize the Sichuan exchange rate, the Chamber received Reply No. 8018 from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, which stated: "Your telegram is acknowledged. Since this Ministry reorganized Sichuan's local currency and established the Central Bank's notes as the standard, the Sichuan exchange rate had already stabilized. Recently, Chongqing's silver and money businesses, due to insufficient funds in circulation, issued 'exchange warrants' for inter-bank transfers. This has caused the Shanghai exchange rate to fluctuate again, contrary to this Ministry's intention to maintain Sichuan's financial stability. We have telegraphed Chairman Chiang and Chairman Liu to strictly order all banks and firms in Chongqing to recall the 'exchange warrants' immediately and prohibit their re-issuance. Simultaneously, we have instructed Chongqing's silver and money businesses to contact the Central Bank and the Bank of China for loans to facilitate the recall. These 'exchange warrants' will be recalled soon, and the Sichuan exchange rate will return to normal. Please inform the Chamber accordingly." This reply.

Scheduled to be held in Guangzhou on the 26th of this month...Public Notice and Meeting Schedule are both Announced

The Municipal Association of Traditional Chinese Medicine: Petitioning for the Promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations

The Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan at its 43rd meeting on December 15th, 1933, but have not been promulgated. National medical organizations have successively submitted petitions urging their promulgation, but without result. Now, it is learned that the Shanghai Municipal Association of Traditional Chinese Medicine has also sent separate telegrams to the Fifth National Congress and the First Plenary Session. Excerpts are as follows: (1) Petition to the Fifth National Congress: Regarding the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations, which have already been passed by the Legislative Yuan, we respectfully request that the case be reviewed and submitted to the National Government for prompt promulgation, so that they may be followed and medical affairs may be emphasized. We believe that traditional Chinese medicine has a history of thousands of years, with remarkable efficacy. Its healing methods have been revered throughout history and remain unchanged. Since the rise of Western medicine in China, a trend has emerged, and many believe in it, resulting in a decline in traditional Chinese medicine, which is lamentable. Those who deeply understand the excellence of traditional Chinese medicine know that it cannot be abandoned, and they deeply believe that it is valued by foreigners. Therefore, some people publicly drafted the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations, which were submitted to the Legislative Yuan and passed last year. However, they have not yet been promulgated and implemented. Now, we respectfully express the views of the members of this association, petitioning the Congress to review the case and submit it to the National Government for prompt promulgation, so that it may be followed and medical affairs may be emphasized. At the same time, it should be incorporated into the education system, so that traditional Chinese medicine becomes a specialized subject for national study. This will allow for gradual progress and further reforms, ensure that traditional Chinese medicine is not neglected, and benefit both the national economy and the people's livelihood. Therefore, we present this document for your review. We respectfully request that the National Government approve its implementation. We are deeply grateful. Sincerely presented. (2) Petition to the First Plenary Session: (Opening omitted) The Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan years ago, but the Executive Yuan has not yet promulgated them, causing public anxiety and uncertainty. At this Fifth National Congress, a resolution was passed to treat both traditional Chinese and Western medicine equally in order to promote scholarship and benefit the people's livelihood, and it was submitted to your Congress for consideration. Regarding the question of whether the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations should be revised, we respectfully request that you promptly pass it, and immediately send the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations to the Executive Yuan of the National Government for prompt promulgation, in order to satisfy public expectations and benefit the people's livelihood. This is a public convenience that we anxiously await.

Public Notice from the Municipal Public Safety Bureau: Smokers to Exchange for Opium Cessation Licenses

Complete the exchange within three months...Licenses not collected by the deadline will be cancelled. The Public Safety Bureau issued a public notice stating: "Smokers, previously, the number of you registered at this Bureau and its various branches was very large, and there was not enough time to fill out the licenses. The licenses are being successively filled out and distributed to the branches for verification and exchange. Now, this Bureau has completed filling out the opium cessation licenses for both the 'ordinary' and 'poor' categories of smokers who registered in the seventh, eighth, ninth, tenth, and eleventh months (of the year), and has issued them to the branches for distribution. It is feared that many of you have moved, making it impossible for the branches to deliver the licenses to the addresses. Therefore, this public notice is issued to inform all smokers who registered before November and hold receipts to bring their receipts to the original registration bureau within this month to exchange them for official licenses. If you fail to collect your licenses by the deadline, they will be cancelled. Do not delay and jeopardize your interests. This notice is issued by Bureau Chief Cai Jingjun."

Five Solar Eclipses This Year: The Last One on the 25th of This Month...But Not Visible in Shanghai or Greenwich

The New Sound Society reports that, according to the Sheshan Observatory, there will be a total of five solar eclipses this year. December 25th to 26th will be the date of the last solar eclipse of the year, a total solar eclipse. There was a partial solar eclipse on January 5th, another partial solar eclipse from February 3rd to 4th, another on July 1st, and another on July 30th. This month, from the 25th to the 26th, will be a total solar eclipse, which is also the last solar eclipse of the year. According to the observatory's calculations using Chinese coastal time, this total solar eclipse will not be visible in Greenwich or Shanghai. The conditions of the eclipse, initial phase, eclipse at first contact (start of central eclipse), the emergence of light (completion of central eclipse), and return to full circle in Wellington, from sunrise, eclipse disappears 0.4.4 to 26th at 1:20, the solar eclipse ends, it is said.

Live Plucking of Pig Bristles Causes Huge Losses: Fresh Pig Industry Refuses to Accept Injured Piglets

Requesting Authorities to Vigorously Prohibit...Notice to Customers to Pay Attention

The Fresh Pig Slaughter Industry Association of this city has stated that, as winter approaches, customers from various regions are shipping pigs that have had their bristles live-plucked by workers. This is very unfavorable to the pigs' survival. Often, the piglets die within a day or two after being injured, resulting in significant business losses. The Sanitation Bureau's inspection also identifies them as diseased pigs, causing substantial financial losses. Therefore, an emergency meeting was convened the other day. As a result of the discussion, it was decided that, starting from the 10th of this month, all pigs that have had their bristles live-plucked will be rejected. A notice was issued yesterday stating: "Notice: Since the beginning of winter, the piglets slaughtered by this industry on behalf of various pig shops in the Nanshi area have had almost all of their bristles live-plucked. Not only is this industry's due profit completely deprived, but also the injured piglets often die soon after slaughter. The meat is red, and the Sanitation Bureau inspectors often identify them as diseased pigs, resulting in losses and grievances. Such extra losses are considerable and unbearable in the long run. Therefore, in order to save the industry from suffering, it was decided at the emergency meeting of this association that, starting from the 10th of this month, this industry will not accept any piglets that have had their bristles live-plucked, in order to avoid losses and reduce suffering. A separate letter has been sent to the Fresh Pig Industry and Fresh Meat Industry Associations for their information. This notice is hereby published in the newspaper. To the Fresh Meat Industry Association: The suffering of the piglets sold by various pig shops in the Nanshi area and slaughtered by our industry due to the live plucking of bristles has already been mentioned above. It is unnecessary to repeat it. It is hereby decided that, starting from the 10th of this month, piglets that have had their bristles live-plucked will not be accepted. If your industry is short of goods for the market, please purchase from Wusong and Yangjing. We are mutually concerned about each other's pain and share the same interests. We hope for your understanding and assistance. A separate letter has been sent to your association for notification. Sincerely, December 7th, 1935."

Huo Zhongbo and Haruyama Bunji were apprehended together by detectives.

Huo Zhongbo, a Cantonese resident of No. 31 Zhixiang Lane, Dongbaoxing Road, Zhabei, has recently been jointly engaged in the business of selling handguns with a Japanese man named Haruyama Bunji. Detectives Zhang Desheng and Liu Longchao of the Jiaxing Road Police Station learned of this, disguised themselves as buyers, contacted Huo, and arranged to meet at Room 11 of the Hongkou Hotel on North Sichuan Road the day before to deliver the guns and ammunition. Russian Owner Kills Russian Partner: Sentenced to Twelve Years of Imprisonment

The owner of the candy and bread store at No. 234-6 Avenue Albert, Russian citizen Bliqiang (transliteration), 48 years old, killed his business partner, Russian citizen Semyanov (transliteration, 30 years old), because Semyanov engaged in indecent behavior with his nine-year-old daughter Lala (transliteration) and seven-year-old daughter Weiliang (transliteration). On the afternoon of the 26th of last month, at 2:00 PM, he called Semyanov upstairs to question him. Because Semyanov not only refused to admit it but also became violent, Bliqiang became overwhelmed with anger and stabbed Semyanov to death with a sharp meat knife, inflicting a total of ten wounds to his throat, abdomen, and arms. Afterward, Bliqiang surrendered himself to the French Police Station. The police transported Semyanov's body to the morgue and reported it to the Second Special District Court, which sent officials to verify the cause of death. Because there were no family members, the body was buried by the Municipal Council's charity organization. Bliqiang was handed over to the Second Special District Court, and the French Police Department filed a public prosecution against him for murder under Article 271 of the Criminal Law. Judge Zhang Chaozu conducted the trial and scheduled the sentencing. All details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang arrived at the First Criminal Division and ordered the defendant to be brought before the court. Bliqiang was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for murder. After the sentencing, the defendant was ordered to be detained in the detention center during the appeal period. After the appeal period, he will be sent to prison to serve his sentence. It is also heard that the defendant is dissatisfied with the verdict and will file an appeal after receiving the judgment.

Chen Changgeng's Invention: Chen-Style Chinese Typewriter: Can Type Horizontally and Vertically

The Datong News Agency reports that Chen Changgeng, a Ningbo native residing at Houde Lane, Pissot Road, has invented a Chinese typewriter that can type horizontally and vertically, recognizing that the inability of Chinese typewriters to do both was a deficiency. He has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry for a patent. Yesterday, this reporter visited Mr. Chen, who was wearing a blue cotton shirt and pants and appeared very simple and honest. According to him, he previously worked at the Yu Binji Typewriter Factory. He realized that Chinese typewriters that could type horizontally could not type vertically, and those that could type vertically could not type horizontally. This was very inconvenient in application. Therefore, he devoted himself to research and finally succeeded after more than five years. However, he intends to continue his research in order to achieve greater precision. He then showed us his completed Chinese typewriter. The machine is horizontal, 18 inches long, 22 inches wide, and 9.5 inches high, weighing approximately 65 pounds. Its special features include: (A) All materials are entirely domestic products; (B) It can type horizontally and vertically; (C) It only requires No. 4 font, which can be used in any printing house; (D) There is no risk of the type bars getting stuck. Therefore, its effectiveness surpasses that of any other Chinese typewriter. The machine is now named the Chen-Style Chinese Typewriter, and he has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry for a patent. He has received Reply No. 13947 from the Ministry of Industry, which states: "Applicant Chen Changgeng has submitted a letter requesting a patent for the typewriter design and specifications submitted in accordance with the order. The letter and attachments have been received. Please report to the Industrial Technology Encouragement Review Committee for review and then submit for approval. There are no restrictions in the regulations on whether items can be manufactured and sold during the patent application period. Please be informed."

Not Hesitating to Labor, Appealing for the Disaster Victims; The Boy Scouts' Universal Donation Results Announced; The Total Amount Reached Over 35,804 Yuan; The Highest Record in the History of Boy Scouts' General Mobilization for Fundraising

First Place in Total Amount by Group: Minli Girls' High School; First Place in Average Amount by Group: Dazhong Middle School; First Place Individually: Qian Yueying from Minli Girls' High School

The Shanghai Relief Association for Flood Victims in Various Provinces, considering the widespread devastation and immense suffering in various regions, and the approaching severe winter making the situation even more critical, deemed it necessary to provide relief to avert the rural crisis and help the disaster victims survive. It consulted and obtained the consent of the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council to launch a city-wide general mobilization of Boy Scouts to raise funds for relief. Li Dachao, Deputy Director of the Fundraising Group of the Flood Relief Association, and Luo Lie, a member of the Boy Scouts Council, were responsible for carrying out the project. A total of 112 groups with 6,700 participants were involved. The general mobilization began on the 9th of last month, lasting for two days externally and one week internally, concluding on the 17th. Details of the efforts were reported in this newspaper. During the fundraising period, rumors were rampant in the city, and some Boy Scouts had to leave school, making it difficult for each group to collect donation tickets and funds. Despite the Boy Scouts Council's strict orders for each group to submit their collections, it was not until the 3rd of this month that all the donations were collected. Due to the large amount, especially the abundance of small coins and fractional notes, the funds were checked and calculated over several days, and the statistics were finally completed yesterday. A total of supplementary coins and fractional notes were collected, amounting to 27,569.55 silver dollars, 96,684.5 small silver dollars, and 56,411 copper coins. According to the legal regulations, 12 small silver dollars are converted into one yuan, and 300 copper coins are converted into one yuan, totaling 35,814.629 national currency silver dollars. This amount has exceeded the previous Boy Scout fundraising record by more than twofold. In the current depressed economic climate, it is not easy to raise such a sum to help the disaster victims. The enthusiasm and generosity of people from all walks of life are truly moving. Mayor Wu of Shanghai, recognizing the Boy Scouts' consistent and commendable service to the disaster victims in the past, specially made 40 silk banners to commend their benevolent spirit and encourage them. All groups ranked in the top ten in terms of total amount, the top ten in terms of average amount per person, and the top twenty individuals in terms of individual amount received a silk banner each. Boy Scout Council members Leng Xueqiao and Luo Lie also presented the "Three Trainings of the Chinese Boy Scouts" (deluxe bound edition), which they had personally compiled. All members ranked in the top twenty in terms of total amount or with an average donation of over seven yuan per person received a deluxe copy of the book. Individuals with donations of over one hundred yuan each received a copy of the book. In addition, the Flood Relief Association and the Council presented each group with certificates and Boy Scout commemorative badges according to regulations to encourage their spirit of service to the community.
