Proving Two Foreign Constables Pushed a Sick Person into the River to Their Death; Two Western Constables Are Accused; Sun Jinsheng's Detailed Account of Rescuing Ma Debiao; The Police File a Fair Lawsuit with the British Court

At 2:45 AM on the 1st of this month, Chinese Constable No. 1728 from the Jiaxing Road Police Station was patrolling the intersection of Xinjihang Road and Zhoujiazui Road when he suddenly saw a man lying on the side of the road, unable to speak and seemingly seriously ill. He immediately reported the information to the police station by telephone. The station then dispatched Western Constables E.W. Peters No. 229 and W.A. Jndd No. 106, along with Chinese Constable No. 3067 as the driver, to the location in a car. They carried the man onto the car and drove to the intersection of Feilun Road and Yalu Road. Suddenly, the two Western constables ordered the driver to stop the car and then threw the man into the river before driving back to the police station. A passerby, Sun Jinsheng, and others witnessed this and immediately devised a way to rescue him. They reported the incident to Chinese Constable No. 993 of the Hongkou Police Station, who sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Unfortunately, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 8:00 AM the day before yesterday. The body was transported to the Feilun Road morgue for examination. After investigating the incident, the Hongkou Police Station found that the two Western constables had violated the law and, on the morning of the 5th, sent them to the British Consulate for legal prosecution. The hearing was postponed to next Tuesday, and they were each released on bail of 200 pounds. The day before yesterday afternoon, the First Special District Court appointed forensic doctors Wei Ligong and Zhang Yan to conduct an autopsy at the morgue together with doctors from the Municipal Council. Yesterday morning around 10:00 AM, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special Court's Prosecutor's Office, along with the two forensic doctors and court clerk Wang Zuyi, came to inspect the body again. They then began the public hearing. First, Western Police Chief Bonner reported the incident. Sun Jinsheng testified that he was 26 years old, a local resident living at No. 493 Feilun Road, and made a living selling vegetables. He said that he went out at 3:00 AM that morning and saw a car parked beside the riverbank. Two Western constables were leaning over the railing, looking into the river. One of them was also shining a flashlight. He noticed that the car was No. 8502. After the two constables got into the car and left, he ran to the riverbank and saw the deceased. He borrowed a bamboo pole from a boat docked on the shore and used it to rescue him. He also shouted for help. Guo Sanyuanzi testified that he was 31 years old, from Gaoyou, lived at No. 491 Feilun Road, and ran a small shop. He said that he was asleep at 3:00 AM that morning when he heard shouts for help. He got up and ran over, and saw Sun Jinsheng had already rescued the deceased. He helped pull him up and saw that the deceased was foaming at the mouth. Chinese Constable No. 3067 testified that he was driving the car at 2:45 AM that morning and saw the two Western constables throw the deceased into the river. Chinese Detective Shi Guichun from the Hongkou Police Station testified that he had investigated at Tongren Hospital and learned from the deceased that he was Ma Debiao, 48 years old, from Nanjing. He had come to Shanghai from his hometown to find a friend but was unsuccessful. Because he had no food to eat, he jumped into the river that day. He seemed confused when he spoke, and his words were slurred. After hearing the testimonies, Prosecutor Guo ruled that the deceased, Ma Debiao, was a male who died from pneumonia before being thrown into the water. According to the police investigation and witness testimonies, the deceased was pushed into the river by the British men Peter and Judd. Since the police have already filed a lawsuit against the two British men with the British Consulate, the case should be handled by the British court. The body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial.

The Continental Daily reported that Mao Debiao, who was injured after being thrown into the Hongkou River on the night of December 1st by two British police chiefs as reported in yesterday's newspaper, died at Tongren Hospital on Friday morning. Since this involves a death, the cause of death is currently being thoroughly investigated. British authorities have refused to comment on Mr. Ma's death, only stating that the case will continue to be heard next Tuesday as originally scheduled.

The Social Affairs Bureau Orders Pawnshops to Temporarily Shorten the Redemption Period and Instructs Each Pawnshop to Submit a Detailed List

The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau issued a written order to the Shanghai Pawnshop Association yesterday, stating: "Regarding the association's request to shorten the redemption period for pawned goods to twelve months, which has been submitted to the Bureau and approved, we have now received Order No. 16113 from the Municipal Government, stating that both requests have been received. The Municipal Pawnshop Association's earlier request to shorten the period has been forwarded to the government by the Bureau. Given the current economic depression and the decline of various industries, to prevent the closure of legitimate shops and indirectly affect the poor who rely on pawnshops, it is temporarily approved to shorten the full redemption period to twelve months. When the economic situation improves, the current regulations will be reinstated. This was resolved at the 290th Municipal Council meeting and approved, and it has been reported to the central government for record. Therefore, you are hereby ordered to inform all members of the association to comply with this order, determine the shortened period, and submit a detailed list of pawnshops that have shortened the period and those that have not, for record." This order is issued.

Regarding the Wang Quan Qu Ying Extortion Case, Three Extortion Cases Were Solved, and the Perpetrators Were Sentenced in Court

Liang Linzhang and Ni Guoxiang's Attempts to Shift Blame Were Futile; Liang Sentenced to One Year and Two Months, Ni to One Year and Six Months

Liang Linzhang, a Cantonese resident of No. 62, Hengde Lane, Hart Road, and Ni Guoxiang, a native of Haimen working as a tea server at Zhang Yougu's house, No. 60, Hart Road, were suspected of writing threatening letters to Wang Quan Qu Ying, a female instructor at Nanjing Jinling University residing at No. 54 in the same lane, demanding 5,000 yuan. They were arrested by Chinese detectives Zhu Mengwei, Gao Huixian, He Errui, and others from the Gordon Road Police Station and brought to the First Special Court for interrogation. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that during the postponement of the case, after a thorough investigation by Chinese and foreign detectives handling the case, it was discovered that Liang and Ni had been plotting to write threatening letters for a long time. Because they were neighbors, they secretly met to discuss plans to extort money. On July 28th of this year, they wrote a threatening letter and sent it to the Shanghai Bank branch on Yuyuan Road, demanding 5,000 yuan and arranging a meeting at the intersection of Xinzha Road and Hart Road. If their demands were not met, they threatened to use bombs or gather more than 20 accomplices to rob the bank. On August 12th, they sent a letter to Li Xingsheng, an assistant at the Public Concession's dispatch office residing at No. 30 in the same lane, extorting 5,000 yuan, threatening to kill his entire family if he refused to pay. On August 29th, they sent a letter to Zhang Shunian, the president of Xinhua Bank on Jing'an Temple Road, demanding 30,000 yuan, arranging a meeting in front of the New World Hotel, threatening to rob the bank and assassinate the president if their demands were not met. After receiving the letters, the victims reported to the police station one after another, requesting investigation. It was not until Liang and Ni were arrested for threatening Wang Quan Qu Ying that the police discovered that the above cases were also committed by them. The handwriting on the threatening letters was also found to be from Liang Linzhang. Yesterday morning, Liang and Ni were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court for further interrogation. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the above circumstances and requested that they be punished according to Article 346, Section 3 of the Criminal Law. Subsequently, Bao Zhengrun, the manager of the Shanghai Bank's Yuyuan Road branch, and Hua Xiehe, the representative of Xinhua Bank's president Zhang Shunian, submitted cases to prove the circumstances of receiving the letters and reporting to the police. When questioned, Liang Linzhang confessed that the matter was initiated and drafted by Ni Guoxiang, who instructed him to copy and deliver the letters. Because he had just arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong and was unfamiliar with the Shanghai dialect, he followed Ni's instructions. Ni Guoxiang only admitted to participating in the Wang Quan Qu Ying extortion case, claiming that he drafted the letter but denied any involvement in the other cases. After reviewing the confessions, Judge Liu Yugui sentenced Liang Linzhang in court to one year and two months in prison for continuous joint attempted extortion, and Ni Guoxiang to one year and six months for the same crime. The threatening letters were confiscated.

Jiuxin Enamel Factory Creates Safe Enamel Stove

Shaanxi Coal Briquettes Are Also Very Convenient, A Home with One Is a Boon Against the Cold

Coal briquette stoves are most common in the north, and almost every household has one because they are inexpensive and convenient to use. In recent years, they have become popular in Shanghai, but sometimes the air does not circulate properly, and carbon dioxide gas remains in the room, which can suffocate people to death. This is a major flaw in the safety of the stove's construction. The Jiuxin Enamel Factory in Nanshi of this city has created a safe enamel coal briquette stove with a legitimate device that eliminates the risk of poisoning. It is coated with enamel, making it clean and beautiful, and it is also extremely convenient to use the heat to cook food and boil water. As the weather is getting colder and stoves are needed, this economical, convenient, and safe coal briquette stove can be said to be a boon against the cold for the masses. The factory also has various enamel coal-saving stoves with beautiful designs and great efficiency, priced low, making them the most suitable household appliances for ordinary families.

Huang Xianyao Forged 100,000 Yuan Note Appeal Case Heard Yesterday, Li Mucheng and Three Other Households Appealed Unsatisfied, Both Courts Must Retrieve Original Records

The First Instance Process

Huang Xianyao, the 31-year-old second son of the late tycoon Huang Chu Jiu, currently residing at No. 53, Rue Pu Shi, French Concession, practices at the China-West Pharmacy. Previously, in an attempt to defraud his father-in-law Zhou Songqing, he colluded with lawyer Mi Jingshen and assistant Wu Jiajin to forge a note stating that Zhou Songqing was holding Huang's property, and that after the matter was concluded, Xianyao's (i.e., Xianyao's) branch should receive 100,000 yuan for independent management. He first submitted it to the Shanghai District Court, requesting mediation with Zhou, but it failed and was shelved. Later, Wang Shaozeng, a creditor of the Gongfa Company, learned of this and obtained a photo of the note. He then filed a private prosecution against Huang Xianyao and Zhou Songqing in the Second Special Court's Criminal Division for destroying creditors' rights, requesting an investigation. Subsequently, six other households, including creditors Shui Jiantang, Shui Cuifeng, Cheng Kefan, Li Zhongxiang, Shui Taiji, and Li Mucheng, joined the private prosecution. Because the defendant Huang Xianyao failed to appear after being summoned, a warrant was issued for his arrest. Later, the court sent personnel to authenticate the photo of the note, and it was recognized as being written by Zhou Songqing, but Zhou firmly denied it. After the court retrieved the original note from the safe deposit box at the Guohua Bank, Zhou Songqing immediately filed a lawsuit with the French police station accusing Huang Xianyao of forging documents. The French police department took Huang into custody for investigation, and Police Vice-Director Rao Boze authenticated the note, confirming that it was not written by Zhou. Huang also confessed that Mi Jingshen, Wu Jiajin, and others had arranged for the writing of the note. The French police department then filed a public prosecution against Huang Xianyao, Mi Jingshen, Wu Jiajin, and others for forging documents, and the private prosecution was suspended. Subsequently, the public prosecution court sentenced Huang Xianyao to one year in prison, suspended for two years. After the sentence was finalized, the private prosecution was continued. As a result, based on the public prosecution's trial process and the authentication report, Huang Xianyao and Zhou Songqing were found not guilty. Later, other creditors filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai District Court accusing Huang and Zhou of destroying evidence and perjury. The case has been concluded, and it has been ruled inadmissible. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper.

Three Creditors Appeal

The creditors Li Mucheng, Li Zhongxiang, and Cheng Kefan expressed dissatisfaction with the Second Special Court's judgment on the private prosecution. They presented reasons and submitted a statement to the Second Special Court's collegiate panel to file an appeal. Yesterday at 3:30 p.m., Judge Zhang Chaozuo opened an investigative court to hear the case. Only the appellant Cheng Kefan, accompanied by his attorney, and Dong Yu, the attorney for Li Zhongxiang and Li Mucheng, appeared in court. The appellees Huang Xianyao and Zhou Songqing also appeared in court with their attorneys Wu Zhiping and Fang Jiazhen. The court first questioned both parties about their ages and origins. According to the appellant Cheng Kefan, he had deposited 3,500 yuan into the Riyue Bank. After seeing the newspaper report about Wang Shaozeng's private prosecution against the appellees for concealing 100,000 yuan in assets, he also joined the private prosecution. The reasons for the appeal are that the original judgment was based on the public prosecution judgment, citing a letter from Wu Jiajin, which recognized the note as forged, but Wu's handwriting was not verified. Moreover, the note had undergone mediation, so it could not be forged. The first instance judgment found the appellees not guilty, so he was dissatisfied and filed an appeal. Cheng's attorney continued, stating that Huang Xianyao had confessed in the original trial that the note was written by Mi Jingshen and Wu Jiajin, but Mi and Wu were not summoned to testify. Now, the appellant has learned that Mi Jingshen is now in Shanghai, residing in Room 10, Dongfang Apartment, Beile Road, and requested that he be summoned. Dong Yu, the attorney for the appellants Li Mucheng and Li Zhongxiang, stated the reasons for the appeal, saying that the handwriting of the 100,000 yuan note had been authenticated in the original trial and matched the handwriting in Zhou's ledger. Later, based on the authentication of a foreign detective in the public prosecution case who did not understand Chinese literature, and ignoring the key points of Huang Xianyao's confession, a judgment was made without further investigation. The appellants believe that this is unacceptable and have filed an appeal, requesting a detailed investigation and requesting that the Gongfa Company's ledger be retrieved from the Gongfa Company's liquidator, accountant Pan Qibang, to verify the handwriting.

Statements of Huang and Zhou

When questioned, Huang Xianyao stated that the note had been authenticated in both the private and public prosecution cases, requesting that the authentication reports be verified. Zhou Songqing is my father-in-law. I first entrusted lawyer Mi Jingshen to handle the case of cohabitation with my wife. Mi and Wu Jiajin suggested that because I wanted to live with my wife but had no money, I should get some money from my father-in-law. Wu Jiajin then asked someone to write the note and requested mediation at the district court, but it failed. They told me to sue again, but I was unwilling. Later, Tang Shouchun asked me for money, but I refused, so he put the note in a safe deposit box and colluded with the creditors to sue me. To investigate the person who wrote this note, it is only necessary to summon Wu Jiajin, and it will be clear. This note is indeed forged. Wu Jiajin wrote me a letter guaranteeing his testimony. This letter is now in the public prosecution case. Please summon Tang Shouchun and Zhu Zishou to testify. Zhou Songqing stated that he did not write this note. Moreover, Huang Chu Jiu never had any money, as everyone knows. This note is completely forged. Xianyao listened to bad people's instigation and requested mediation at the district court. I originally wanted to pursue the matter, but Xianyao's mother and my daughter pleaded with me, so I did not investigate deeply, which led to the current entanglement. How could such an important matter as 100,000 yuan be written on a mere note? The note has been clearly authenticated and is definitely forged. The original trial was very fair. The appellants' appeal shows that they are fond of litigation. Please reject the appeal and uphold the original judgment based on the facts and evidence. Zhou's attorney, Wu Zhiping, stated that the appellants' attorney said that the original trial adopted the authentication of a foreigner who did not understand Chinese literature, which was insufficient to convince. However, the authentication report of the original trial was also inconsistent, and the court should pay attention to this. According to Huang Xianyao's defense attorney, regarding the 100,000 yuan note, the public prosecution had already ruled, and Huang Xianyao had been sentenced to imprisonment, which has been finalized. Therefore, this case has already been concluded. At the end, the lawyers for both sides expressed their opinions. The court ordered that the case file be retrieved from the Shanghai District Court, and the District Court also retrieved the case file from this court. After the case files are retrieved, a hearing will be scheduled. The court was then adjourned.

Hong Yaoyu, Employee of Baocheng Silver Shop, Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea

The Deceased Was from Cixi, Leaving Behind a Will Expressing Dissatisfaction with His Uncle

Datong News Agency reports that the Taigu New Beijing Ship sailed from Shanghai to Ningbo at 5 p.m. on the 4th. At midnight that day, the ship was passing through the waters of Daji Mountain when another young passenger committed suicide by jumping into the sea. The details are as follows:

Suicide by Jumping into the Sea at Midnight: The New Beijing Ship left Shanghai for Ningbo at 5 p.m. on the 4th. At that time, a young passenger was traveling in cabin No. 21 on the second deck of the ship. When the ship left Wusong Port, the ship served dinner as usual. The passenger claimed to be unwell and did not eat. He then changed into a bathrobe and went to sleep. At about 11 p.m. midnight, he left his bunk and went outside. The tea attendant Zhang Shide, who was in charge of the cabin, thought he was going to the toilet. However, he did not return for a long time. He was searched, and a bathrobe and shoes were found abandoned on the side of the ship, which confirmed that he had committed suicide by jumping into the sea.

A Glimpse of the Remains: The incident was reported to the purser, who inspected the remains. They included a suitcase (full of clothes), leather shoes, a harmonica, and loose banknotes and silver coins, as well as six letters of testament. After reading them, it was learned that the deceased's name was Hong Yaoyu, 22 years old, from Hongtang Town, Cixi, and that he worked at the Baocheng Gongji Silver Shop on Rue Fada in this city. The letters were all written with addresses and have been sent separately by the ship's tea attendant. The content of the letters cannot be recorded, but it is known that they were addressed to his mother, his sister, Ye Zhuotang, the Baocheng Silver Shop, his uncle, and one letter was left for the ship's staff.

Complaints and Resentment in the Will: The following is an excerpt from his letter to the ship's staff: "To whom it may concern: I have been forced to jump into the sea because of the harm caused by my uncle. Please deliver the belongings left behind to Hong Yaoshan's home in Hongtang Old Residence, Ningbo. I will repay your kindness in the next life. Thank you for your trouble. Sincerely, I wish you a pleasant winter. To all the gentlemen in charge, Hong Yaoyu's last words."

Should Shipping Notices and Other Items Be Affixed with Stamps? Bean and Rice Industry Requests Explanation

Dagong News Agency reports that the Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association has requested the former Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau to exempt the shipping notices, bale sheets, and rice straw sheets used by its members from stamp duty. Since the promulgation of the new Stamp Tax Law, inspectors have also inspected and punished these items, causing great panic among members. Therefore, the association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting the Ministry of Finance to provide an explanation, and separately sent letters to the court and the Municipal Public Security Bureau to suspend enforcement. The original letter and notice are recorded as follows:

Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: "We respectfully inform you that the shipping notices, bale sheets, and rice straw sheets used by our association members have always been used for notification and verification of quantities, and their nature does not belong to the category of loan tickets and receipts. They were approved by the former Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau in the 20th year of the Republic of China to be exempt from stamp duty. The Stamp Tax Law implemented on September 1st of this year, according to Article (blank) Section 9, should also not be subject to stamp duty. However, fearing misunderstandings during the change, inspectors may misunderstand. On August 23rd, we prepared a letter explaining the reasons, attaching samples of the above three types of notes, and requested your association to interpret and reply. We received a reply stating that the proposal to maintain the exemption from stamp duty for shipping notices, etc., has been forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for approval, etc. Unexpectedly, while awaiting approval from the Ministry, stamp inspectors have been inspecting the use of these notes and imposing penalties from the court. If an explanation is not given promptly and clearly, the damage to members will be immeasurable. We are requesting your association to telegraph the Ministry for approval and follow the instructions. We have also separately sent letters to the Public Security Bureau and the District Court to suspend inspections and penalties before the Ministry's approval is received. Respectfully, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association."

Notice to Members: "We respectfully inform you that the shipping notices, bale sheets, and rice straw sheets used by members have always been approved by the former Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau in the 20th year of the Republic of China to be exempt. According to Article 3, Section 9 of the current Stamp Tax Law, demanding overdue payments or verifying the number of account statements, is exempt from stamp duty, which is consistent with the regulations and should not be subject to stamp duty. However, for the sake of caution, the association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry for explanation, but approval has not yet been received. Stamp inspectors have been inspecting these notes and forwarding them to the court for penalty. The association specifically sent another letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting that it immediately telegraph the Ministry for approval, and separately sent letters to the Public Security Bureau and the District Court to suspend inspections and penalties before the Ministry's approval is received. Please take note of this notice. December 7, 24th year of the Republic of China."

Mixed Loading of Vegetable Oil and Other Oils with Kerosene, Charging Methods for Whole Cars

The Ministry of Railways yesterday issued an order to the two-way Management Bureau stating, "According to the Daoqing Railway Management Bureau's Zongzi No. 358 letter of October 13, regarding the Tianjin Asia Petroleum Company's inquiry about whether various single oils can be mixed with kerosene in whole cars and the freight rates to be paid, the Transportation Department of the Bureau signed that there are no clear regulations for mixing ordinary goods with dangerous goods in whole cars, requesting that it be forwarded for interpretation. A copy of the original letter and attachment is attached for your review and instructions." The requests in this regard are hereby stipulated as follows: (1) Rosin oil is a dangerous good for which transportation is not guaranteed and cannot be mixed with kerosene; (2) Vegetable oil, machine oil, asphalt, grease oil, insecticide, candles, wax, empty iron cans, and empty wooden boxes can be mixed with kerosene, and the freight rate is calculated according to the 20th class; (3) Fertilizer can also be mixed with kerosene, but it must be packed in iron barrels or iron cans and sealed. The freight rate is calculated according to the 2nd class. In addition to instructions, it is hereby ordered that the Railway Bureau comply with this order, and the Bureau has forwarded it to the Vehicle Department for compliance.

The approval document is recorded below, omitting the beginning. Previously, the citizen raised an objection regarding the silver light bulb that Li Qingxiang applied for a patent for. Li Qingxiang was instructed to respond, and the matter was forwarded to the Industrial Technology Review Committee for further review. Now, according to the committee's review results, the objection is valid. After review and verification, there is no difference. In addition to notifying Li Qingxiang, the review decision is hereby copied and issued, and you should comply. From now on, no matter which factory it is, all can manufacture silver light bulbs.

At this time of currency inflation, the prices of raw materials continue to rise, and the cost of capital is excessively high, making it increasingly difficult to sustain operations. If we do not promptly devise remedies, we will be on the verge of collapse. The current reorganization of the association is aimed at overcoming difficulties, revitalizing the business of colleagues, and promoting benefits. Adjusting dyeing prices externally and revising industry regulations internally are serious tasks and significant responsibilities. As a pillar of our industry, you have long enjoyed popular support. You have been known for resolving difficulties and disputes without complaint, and you possess a deep enthusiasm that we all admire. It has been unanimously decided at the discussion meeting held on November 28th that "the initial reorganization involves numerous complexities, and we rely on your talent to grasp the key points. We cannot bear to see a veteran general retire into seclusion, seeking only peace. We unanimously support your coming out of retirement, relying on your planning to courageously accept the difficulties." We have specially dispatched Tan Borong and Hu Xiongqing to deliver a letter, urging you to take office and assist in the work. For the sake of the "industry" and "hometown," create benefits for "colleagues." For the sake of "friendship" and "self," seek benefits. Public and private sentiments intersect, which will truly benefit the overall plan. We humbly request that you grant our request in order to save the declining industry. We await with anticipation.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather around Shandong and the Yellow Sea is colder, with strong cyclones, rain or snow, caused by a low pressure system passing and moving northeast-east. The Yangtze River basin is cloudy and turning colder, with strong northwest to north winds. The East China Sea and Taiwan are cloudy, with southeast to northeast winds. The typhoon center at 2:00 PM yesterday had advanced to within about 120 miles of 17 degrees north latitude and 132 degrees east longitude, and was stationary or moving very slowly. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 67.5 and the lowest was 48.2. On the same day last year, the highest was 54.1 and the lowest was 30.2.

Educational News

Jiangsu Education Department and Shanghai Banking Industry Conclude Educational Loan

Totaling 210,000 Yuan with a Monthly Interest Rate of Nine Percent Guaranteed by Wuxian Business Tax and Brokerage Tax

The Jiangsu Provincial Government Education Department recently negotiated with the Shanghai banking industry to borrow 210,000 yuan for the relocation and construction of the Provincial Nanjing Middle School. The payment has been made yesterday. The details are as follows:

Loan Purpose: The Jiangsu Provincial Government Education Department has established many middle schools in the province, with the Nanjing Middle School in the capital being the largest in scale. However, there is no complete middle school in Zhenjiang, the provincial capital. The department believes that the capital has many middle schools in recent times, which can accommodate students. There is no need to establish one, but in the provincial capital, there are very few complete middle schools, and residents often send their children to study in other ports. Therefore, there is a decision to relocate the Provincial Nanjing Middle School in the capital to Zhenjiang, the provincial capital. A loan of 210,000 yuan has been negotiated with the Shanghai banking industry to cover the construction costs of the school buildings.

Successful Negotiation: Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department, who is a member of the Central Committee, came to Shanghai last month to negotiate a loan with the Shanghai banking industry. The loan was undertaken by seven banks: Central, China, Communications, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, Jiangsu, and Jiangsu Farmers. After several consultations between the two parties, the progress was smooth because the amount was not large. The contract was formally signed at the end of last month. Each bank borrowed 30,000 yuan, totaling 210,000 yuan, with a monthly interest rate of 9%. Zhou immediately left Shanghai and returned to the province. It is reported that the Zhong, Zhong, and Jiao banks have telegraphed their Zhenjiang branches yesterday to make the payment on the spot.

One-Year Repayment: This loan will be repaid in one year. The Jiangsu Education Department will use the business tax and brokerage tax of Wuxian as the first guarantee, and the old land and property of Nanjing Middle School in the capital as the second guarantee. As for the new school buildings in Zhenjiang, the Education Department has designed and bid for construction, and it is expected to be completed within one year, at which time it can be moved in.

Today's Education Broadcast Program by Ministry of Education

Topic: The Essence of Nationalism

Lecturer: Dian Zhen

Time: 6:30 PM to 7:00 PM

Today's National Music Academy New Campus Completion Ceremony

The National Music Academy of this city has been in operation for eight years since its founding in 1927. This spring, it finally purchased a site behind the City Hall on Shijing Road in the city center area and began construction. Now it is completed and a completion ceremony will be held today (Sunday) at 2 p.m., along with the Eighth Anniversary Student Concert. Because the school's auditorium is not yet under construction due to limited funds, the meeting will be held in the small auditorium today. Guests must present invitations to be seated, in order to restrict attendance.

School Building Proposal (Xiao Youmei)

(1) Construction Costs: When the plan to establish the Music Academy was submitted to Cai Yuanpei, President of the University Council, in October 1927, the National Government had not been established for long, and there was no guarantee of educational funding, so there was no talk of school building construction. At that time, the University Council reluctantly approved the preparations, and in addition to issuing 2,600 yuan for start-up costs, the government only promised to plan for and issue equipment fees and school site funds after the end of the civil war. From 1937 to July 1935, the school buildings were all rented private houses in the French Concession, and moved four times between 1928 and 1931. We felt that renting residential buildings was absolutely unsuitable for running a music academy, so we submitted new budgets to the government every year, requesting funds for address and construction costs. It was not until 1934 that one-fifth (i.e., 80,000 yuan) of our requested 400,000 yuan was approved. Because this meager 80,000 yuan was insufficient for building a proper school building, a request for an increase in the budget was submitted in 1934, and an additional 40,000 yuan was approved, but only 20,000 yuan had been received as of November of this year.

(2) Selection of School Site: Before 1933, the school affairs meeting had passed a resolution to purchase a site near Zhaofeng Park in the city for the school's base. However, due to the high land price there, it was impossible to purchase it. Later, the 52nd school affairs meeting overturned the resolution and decided to build in the city center. Since the City Hall and various bureaus moved there, and there are also great buildings such as libraries, museums, sports fields, and city hospitals, everyone recognizes that the area is the cultural district of Shanghai. Therefore, the school affairs meeting recently overturned the old plan, and not only did the school's colleagues have no objection, but it was deeply approved by the Ministry of Education and the City Government. The school originally planned to take 30 mu of land, but because it could not pay the land price in full at one time, it temporarily took 16 mu at the end of Shijing Road (behind the City Hall), paid one-quarter of the land price first, and the remainder was to be paid in three years. There was no road there, but after the school paid the land price, the City Government ordered the Bureau of Public Works to specially open a new road for it (i.e., the eastern section of Shijing Road), and also ordered the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to install water pipes and utility poles, so the school had water and electricity soon after construction started. For this point alone, the school expresses its gratitude to the City Government.

(3) First Phase of Construction Plan: The school's construction is carried out in two phases, and architect Mr. Luo Bangjie is commissioned to design and supervise the construction. The estimated cost of the first phase of the construction plan is approximately as follows: (1) Land of approximately 16 mu, approximately 39,290.00 yuan, (2) One main school building (excluding the auditorium), including heating pipes, sanitary equipment, electrical engineering, school roads, and sewers, approximately 87,192.69 yuan, (3) Two practice rooms (17 rooms each), including electrical engineering, approximately 15,900.00 yuan, (4) One dormitory each for male and female students, including sanitary equipment and electrical engineering, approximately 35,600.00 yuan, (5) South-facing wall, 1,985.85 yuan, (6) One kitchen, 800.00 yuan, (7) Architect's design and supervision fees (calculated at 4%), approximately 5,658.46 yuan, (8) Backfilling, approximately 5,000.00 yuan, (9) Cement pillars and bamboo fences on the east, west, and north sides, approximately 3,573.00 yuan, (10) Planting grass and trees, approximately 5,000.00 yuan. The total cost is approximately 200,000 yuan or more. The first phase of the plan is not very large, but it is impossible to fully realize it with only the 100,000 yuan received. Fortunately, Master Yang Sen of Sichuan donated 10,000 yuan to the school for land costs, so the school was able to pay one-quarter of the land fee. In addition, the school's savings from past years, together with sporadic donations, are sufficient to build a practice room. Therefore, during this construction period, only one main school building, two practice rooms, the wall, and the kitchen can be completely completed. Although the women's dormitory has been started, there is no guarantee that it can be completed without funds. Other items such as architect's fees, backfilling, and bamboo fences can only be partially paid for. As for the men's dormitory, it is impossible to start construction, and planting grass and trees is out of the question. In short, to complete the first phase of the school's construction plan (including land price), another 60,000 yuan is needed. We sincerely hope that the government will issue another picture of the front of the new Music Academy school building in the near future, and especially hope that people in society will donate generously. The most important thing about the construction of music school buildings is soundproofing. The school's main building was originally planned to be built with three layers of reinforced concrete, but because the cost was too high, and could not be done without 140,000 or 150,000 yuan, it was changed to three "false" layers, so there is no absolute soundproofing between the second and third floors. The classrooms on the first and second floors can only use cheaper soundproofing equipment, because of economic limitations.

(4) Second Phase of Construction Plan: As for the second phase of the school's construction plan, it includes the following items: (1) 14 mu of land (purchased behind the school), (2) One auditorium, (3) Two more dormitories each for men and women, (4) Two practice rooms, (5) One library, (6) One gymnasium, (7) One faculty dormitory, (8) Four residences for the principal and directors, (9) Architect's design and supervision fees, (10) Backfilling, school roads, sewers, planting grass and trees, (11) Bamboo fences. Whether 200,000 yuan can be used to handle all of the above items is still unknown, but we must have a complete plan. If the economy does not allow it to be realized at the same time, we have to proceed step by step. We deeply hope that music lovers inside and outside the school will work hard to help, so that the school's construction plan can be completed as soon as possible, and music education can be revived, which will have a significant impact on our country's cultural future.

School History, by Fu Shu

Our country's music education has never received special attention. At best, music departments are only appendages of various schools. The establishment of our country's music academies started with this school. The author dares not use this statement to boast, nor dares to be complacent about it, but the difficulty of creation is worth mentioning, so I write this brief history to inform the people of the country. Before the summer vacation of 1927, the music education entrusted to the Music Training Institute attached to Peking University and the Music Department of the Art Academy were both in danger of being destroyed along with the proposal to merge the nine national schools. Fortunately, our National Government was established in Nanjing, and thanks to the wisdom of the authorities, the plan to establish the National Music Academy proposed by Mr. Xiao Youmei was approved, and Mr. Xiao was the chief preparer. However, at that time, the government was focusing on the Northern Expedition, and the national treasury was quite stretched, so only 2,600 yuan was allocated for preparatory expenses to cover all equipment and housing costs. After many difficulties, a school building was rented on Route Paul Henry, and it was named the National Music Academy, with Cai Yuanpei, President of the University Council, concurrently serving as the President. Enrollment was held in early November, and the opening ceremony was held on the 27th of the same month. Thus, the Music Academy, which was unprecedented in China, was officially established. However, because enrollment was too late, only 22 students were admitted the first time. In December of that year, President Cai, due to the many affairs of the University Council, had no time to take care of it, so he specially entrusted Mr. Xiao Youmei, the Dean of Academic Affairs of the Academy, to act as the President of the Academy.

In February 1928, new students were added, and the total number of new and old students was about 56. The school moved to Avenue Joffre and added dormitories. In June of the same year, a new budget for 1928 was submitted and approved by the University Council. From September, the monthly expenses increased to 5,000 yuan, and the number of students also increased to 80. In August of the same year, the school moved again to Rue Pichon and rented a house in Taoyuan Village on Avenue Lafayette, which was the third move of the school. In September, the University Council appointed Mr. Xiao as the President of the Academy.

In July 1929, the National Government amended the University Organization Law. Because the organization law did not have provisions for music and art academies, it ordered the reorganization of the Hangzhou Art Academy into an art academy and this academy into a music academy. Mr. Xiao resigned from his position as President of the Academy to the Ministry of Education. In August, the Ministry of Education reappointed Mr. Xiao as the President of the school, until now. The Music Academy initially had preparatory courses, specialized courses, elective courses, and special elective courses. The preparatory course was a preparation for the elective course and required 60 credits to graduate. The purpose of the specialized course was to train music teachers and required 100 credits. The elective course was designed for those who specialize in one subject and was divided into elementary, middle, and high levels, with 10 credits as the standard for each level. The special elective course was designed for those who aspire to study music but are limited by regulations or are left out due to full quotas and cannot be inserted into each class. Teachers charge different tuition fees for each class, but the selected courses generally attend classes with other classes, so the level is no different from the elective courses. After the reorganization in August 1929, the Ministry of Education ordered that the specialized course be changed to a normal course. In August of the same year, Mr. Shen Zhongjun was hired as the Director of General Affairs. In October, Ms. Hu Zhou Shuan was hired as the Director of the Vocal Music Department, Mr. Zakharoff (disciple of Mr. B. Zakharoff Godowsky, Russian) as the Director of the Piano Department, and Mr. A. Foa (Italian) as the Director of the Violin Department. The vocal music, piano, and violin departments were formally established. At the same time, Mr. Huang Zi, a Bachelor of Music from Yale University, was hired as a theory teacher, and the school affairs were revitalized. In December, the school signed a contract with the Shanghai Commercial Press to publish the school's series of books and the Music Art Quarterly.

In February 1930, the school established a cello department and hired Mr. Shevtzpff (Russian) as the Director of the Cello Department. At that time, because the school's students were progressing very quickly, a research department was added, which was later renamed the research class by order of the Ministry of Education in May. Previously, the school did not have many students, and the academic affairs were relatively simple, so the position of Dean of Academic Affairs was concurrently held by President Xiao. From August of the same year, Mr. Huang Zi was hired as the Dean of Academic Affairs to be solely responsible. In September, the Theory and Composition Department was established, and President Xiao concurrently served as the Director of the Department. Mr. Liao Qingzhu was hired as the editor of the Music Art Quarterly. The first issue was published in April of that year. The school's series of books were also published one after another. The school's affairs had entered the right track, but the school building on Rue Pichon was taken back by the owner in August 1931, so the school moved again to Avenue Lafayette. This was the fourth move of the school. In October of the same year, the Ministry of Education ordered that the preparatory course be changed to a high school class, and the normal course be changed to a high school normal course, both accepting high school graduates. Each department of the undergraduate course was changed to a group, and a normal group was added to the undergraduate course. Graduates of the high school normal course can be promoted to the undergraduate course if they wish to continue their studies, but the number of credits they must complete is set at 40. The remaining theory and composition, piano, violin, cello, vocal music, and Chinese music groups of the undergraduate course must complete 80 credits to graduate. In October of the same year, a refresher course was also established, enrolling beginners in music, taught by normal students for practice. In that year, six kinds of school books had been published. When the January 28th Incident broke out, the school's series of books on harmony and the seventh issue of the Music Art Quarterly were destroyed by artillery fire along with the Commercial Press. The school's publishing plan had to be temporarily suspended. At the same time, because the unpaid expenses had reached four months, the school affairs meeting decided to suspend the dormitory from February. Since then, the school struggled to support itself in the storm. When the overall situation stabilized slightly in 1933, the school's series of books continued to be published at the Commercial Press. As of now, 19 kinds have been published, and there are still six kinds in print. In the same year, the school's staff and students, seeing the need to form a society, reorganized the former Music Art Society, and invited Mr. Cai Yuanpei and Mr. Ye Xia'an to be the presidents. After its establishment, the first plan was to publish a music magazine. After many twists and turns, it was published in Liangyou Company in 1934.

In July 1934, the Director of General Affairs, Mr. Shen Zhongjun, resigned due to personal reasons, and Mr. Chen Nengfang succeeded him. Since then, the school has developed all school affairs, and has tried its best to build school buildings. The school's request for temporary expenses was approved by the Central Political Council for 80,000 yuan. The school used this fund and the 11,200 yuan raised over the years to purchase 16 mu of land on Shijing Road in the city center of Shanghai this spring to build school buildings. However, it was ultimately limited by funds. Currently, only the main school building and the west practice room and the east practice room have been completed, and the women's dormitory is still under construction (before the dormitory is completed, this year, six post office buildings were temporarily rented in Youting Lane on Shilin Road in the city center for use as male and female dormitories). The construction costs for other buildings such as the men's dormitory, library, and gymnasium are still to be raised.

This autumn, the school started with a new life. The school's organization outline and school regulations were revised. The piano group, including the organ, was changed to the keyboard instrument group. The violin group and the cello group were merged into the orchestra instrument group. Mr. Farriguo was the director of the group. At the same time, the Student Affairs Office was formally established (previously, the student affairs were handled by the Student Affairs Committee), and Mr. Huang Guoliang was hired as the acting Director of Student Affairs. In addition, Mr. Li Weining, Mr. Wu Bochao, and Ms. Xiao Shuxian were hired as teachers of the school. All three teachers studied in Europe and returned with honors. In order to popularize music education, the school recruited students from all provinces and regions this academic year. As a result, as many as 15 provinces and regions were recommended by the provincial education halls to take the exam. Gansu and Shaanxi, which have never had anyone come to study, also sent people to take the exam. From now on, there is hope that music teachers will gradually become popular. In terms of professors, the fixed pitch name method is implemented. Elementary vocal music and piano are taught in the whole class, which belongs to the new experiment. Schools should recruit both Chinese and foreign students. The school has also been instructed by the Ministry of Education to generously admit students. Therefore, in February 1932, nearly 20 foreign students applied for the exam. However, the school has limited places and cannot admit too many students. Subsequently, the school affairs meeting decided to temporarily set the number of foreign students to one-tenth of the total number of students. This year, it was changed to two students per group, and there were quite a few people who were left out due to full quotas. It can be seen that the school is valued by Chinese and foreign people.

As for the school's formally graduated students, although there are not many (three undergraduates, seven undergraduates in the normal group, two high school normal students, and two elective students), they all have considerable jobs after graduation. In addition, there is a shortage of musical talents in the country, so there are often students who study at the school for two or three years and leave to take jobs without graduating. Among the 137 students currently studying at the school, 20 or 30 are already working outside the school (or teaching in universities, vocational schools, and primary and secondary schools in this city, or composing music for film companies, or as tutors). It can be seen that the demand for musical talents exceeds the supply, so that most students leave the school to work before graduating, which is also a clear proof that those who study music do not have to worry about finding a way out.

Xiao Youmei, President of the Music Academy

Yesterday's Jiangda Football Match, Jinan Guanghua Draw, Zero to Zero Each Unsuccessful, Jinan Missed Penalty

Jiangda Football Tournament, only three teams joined this session: Jinan, Fudan, and Guanghua. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30, Jinan and Guanghua played their first game at Guanghua Stadium on West Road. The result was zero to zero, and each was unsuccessful. Guanghua has always been at a disadvantage. It is fortunate that it was not defeated. After entering the game, both sides kicked off, and their actions were out of line. It seems that this is not an evil habit that people in higher education should have. Moreover, students watching from the sidelines should not hiss and shout. I hope you will pay more attention to this in the future. Here is a record of the game.

Ratio Melee

Referee Shen Huichun blew the whistle to start the game. Guanghua kicked off first. Within a minute, Jinan committed a foul and was awarded a free kick. It was intercepted in the middle and launched a major attack. One pass and one block, the momentum was vast. Guanghua's inner guards were strong. After receiving the ball, they resumed the advance and attacked section by section. The two sides fought in melee for a long time, each without success. After the winter rain, the ground was slightly slippery. Guanghua took advantage of the terrain and frequently oppressed. Before long, Jinan was familiar with the ground and bravely moved forward, repeatedly attacking in front of Guanghua's goal. The situation was very dangerous. After that, the ball often hovered in Guanghua's hinterland. Fortunately, Guanghua's inner guards ran around to deal with it and were spared. Guanghua occasionally got a chance and launched a counterattack, but unfortunately the forwards were weak and could not use it, and missed it. Dong Shuzhao left the field due to injury. Although Jinan's defenders were brave and good at fighting, the cooperation of the forwards was poor, often delaying and missing, or the connection was inaccurate, or the position was uneven, and there were very few opportunities to kick the goal. The first half ended with zero to zero.

Jinan Misses Opportunity

After changing places, everyone believed that Jinan would win. After kicking off, it drove straight in, and its arrogance was terrifying. Guanghua's defender Zhao Aisheng kicked his feet into the air, but Jinan's response was ineffective and failed to achieve anything. It attacked again and again, but still had no chance. It went straight to Huanglong, but Guanghua was forced to approach Jinan's goal from the left, creating a momentary panic. After that, Jinan realized that the past failures were due to too many passes on the defense line, which missed the opportunity. It changed its plan and used shooting. Sure enough, the horns of Hujia were ringing in front of Guanghua's goal. Jinan kicked more than a dozen corner kicks one after another, but they were all intercepted by Guanghua. Although Guanghua occasionally counterattacked, it was only a flash in the pan. Jinan's midfielder Liang Shutang ran all over the field and was the most hardworking. Unfortunately, Wang Nanzhen missed the opportunity in front of the goal, and Zhong Yuxiang's penalty kick was blocked. Although he cheered up and repeatedly oppressed the enemy's goal, the great opportunities all turned into fleeting clouds. As a result, the game ended with a score of zero to zero again. Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (117)

— Louisa M. Alcott original Zheng Xiaocang translation

For a moment, Nan En's heart almost stopped; with her usual courage, thinking of a real bear, she didn't feel like a game, she was about to turn around and run away in a panic, when she suddenly heard a gentle moo, which turned her overwhelming fear into laughter. So she said:

"It's a cow, Robert! The good black cow we saw this afternoon."

The cow also felt strange how she could meet two children in her pasture at night, so this good-tempered and smart animal also stopped to find out. She let them stroke it, standing there and watching them, she showed such gentle eyes, so Nan En, who was afraid of anything but black bears, suddenly decided to get her milk.

"Lai Siwu taught me how to milk; berry stalks mixed with milk are so delicious," she said, and then she poured everything in her bucket into her hat, and boldly started her new job, while Robert stood beside her, following her orders, singing the following song:

"Fat and beautiful cow,

Give us five pecks of fresh milk,

Give us five pecks of fresh milk,

We also want a hundred acres of vanilla from you."

He sang as hard as he could, but it was still useless, because the cow's milk had just been taken, so there was only a spoonful to give to these two thirsty children.

Finance: Gold Market Quiet as Still Water in the First Half of the Day; Fluctuating by One Yuan and Two Jiao in Three Hours; Closing Price Unchanged from Previous Close

The gold market was even more sluggish yesterday, with market conditions remaining stable. There was only a fluctuation of one yuan and two jiao in half a day. From the opening in the morning to the closing at noon, there were only a few jiao of struggle in between. As a result, there was no gain or loss compared to the previous close. In the early morning, overseas silver markets in both the UK and the US were flat. The forward silver price in Monterrey remained unchanged, with some contracting by one li and others rising by one li. Exchange rates all fell, while the French franc strengthened. The price of raw gold in London rose by half a penny. The Central Bank's announced listing showed that both the UK and the US were flat, and the customs gold unit remained unchanged. The standard gold price was listed as 1146.6 yuan, opening slightly higher. After opening, it weakened slightly, but buyers were still enthusiastic. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's announced listing showed that both the UK and the US were flat, indicating extremely peaceful conditions. Later, due to the sudden selling interest of a certain retail investor, the price once fell to within four yuan. Unexpectedly, major players Yifeng Yongqingfa Yong successively purchased, and it was soon pulled up. The silver equalization tax was announced as unchanged, and it still had no impact. At this time, a certain retail investor went short, and the price once rose slightly to five yuan. Major player Fuxingyong took the opportunity to sell high, and the price gradually fell again. However, buyers took the opportunity to maintain the price, and the foreign exchange market was also stable. In the end, it hovered between 4.2 yuan and 4.6 yuan, and it was difficult to change. The prediction for the Indian silver market was unchanged. The afternoon was even calmer. The swap rate was posted by the bulls at around eight yuan yesterday. At present, the number of January contracts has decreased to more than 11,700, and the bulls are only four more than the bears. Grain: Powder Market Remains in Turmoil

Yesterday, the powder market opened in the morning with extreme disorder across all months. Quotations for foreign wheat ranged from eight to ten points in Chicago and fell by four to ten points in Canada. At the opening, due to the lack of significant fluctuations in foreign wheat and the unconfirmed news from the previous day, market sentiment revived. Buying interest surged across all months, causing prices to jump by three to four points. However, the market suddenly changed drastically at the start of the second session, with large players aggressively liquidating long positions. Rumors of a certain bank's commissioned selling led to widespread panic and exhaustion, causing prices to fall by three to four points from the opening. Subsequently, near-term contracts continued to fall, while distant contracts showed some stabilization. The difference between the opening and closing prices for the current month reached a significant six and a quarter points due to the absence of customer draws. At the opening in the afternoon, the market was initially still poor, but new short positions halted and factory activity lessened, gradually improving sentiment by one to two points from the lowest level. Future fluctuations will continue to depend on news from abroad.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, continuous strong arrivals from various routes down the river totaled about 65-66 firms. Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

The Strong Eat the Weak

— Ning Ziqiang

Children, since the dissemination of Darwin's theory of evolution from England, we have generally recognized "survival of the fittest, the strong eat the weak" as the axiom of natural selection. However, facts tell us that not only do the strong eat the weak, but sometimes the weak eat the strong. Let's first establish a "hypothesis" and then provide some proof!

1. Hedgehogs Eat Tigers: "The fierce tiger in the deep mountains strikes fear into the hearts of all beasts!" However, the tiger, fond of meat, sometimes "doesn't have time to choose" and will "run into a nail." The hedgehog is the tiger's nemesis. If it encounters a tiger, it will curl up into a ball, allowing the tiger to swallow it whole. But once swallowed, it will unleash its might and slowly chew on the tiger's internal organs.

2. Ants Trap Mantises: The mantis is many times larger than an ant. Yet, within inches, it is trapped by ants and unable to move, eventually being eaten by the ants.

Children! From these two examples, we learn that relying on intelligence and collective strength are the only strategies for small nations to cope with powerful nations!

Pei Xingjian's Forgiveness Towards Others

— Wei Bingxin

Pei Xingjian of the Tang Dynasty was a famous general who understood military strategy and was good at recognizing talent. Although he had always lived among soldiers, he was kind and forgiving and completely lacked the rude habits of military men.

At that time, disturbances broke out in the Great Food Nation (Arab Caliphate), and Emperor Gaozong specially appointed Xingjian as the pacification envoy to survey and resolve the situation. After receiving the order, Xingjian led a troop, traveled tens of thousands of miles, and finally quelled the rebellious party, establishing a remarkable achievement. When he returned in triumph, the king of the Great Food Nation specially selected many pearls and treasures to give him as souvenirs.

Those treasures were all very valuable items. Xingjian brought them back and carefully hid them, never willing to easily show them to others. One day, he hosted a banquet for his subordinate generals and ordered a guard to bring out those treasures and display them in the hall for public appreciation.

Among them was a most valuable agate plate, more than two feet in diameter, with very elegant patterns, which was Xingjian's favorite object. Unexpectedly, while the guard Wang Xiulie was carrying this agate plate up the stairs to the hall, he stumbled due to carelessness, his left foot catching on the hem of his robe, causing him to fall. The agate plate he was holding crashed against the stone steps and shattered into pieces.

Wang Xiulie, having caused this disaster, was naturally terrified. He immediately kowtowed before Xingjian, begging for forgiveness, even breaking the skin on his forehead and causing it to bleed.

If it were another military man, upon seeing a guard destroy his beloved object, he would at least scold him, or even flog him. However, Xingjian was usually kind and forgiving and did not have the habits of ordinary military men. He remained calm and said kindly, "Get up quickly! — The plate is broken, so be it; you didn't break it on purpose, why do you need to do this?"

Good baby, get up early, be energetic all year round!

Singing makes your heart blossom,

Eating fills your belly,

All these rewards,

Are all because you get up early!

Get up early! Get up early! Be healthy and happy!

Get up early! Get up early! Be free from worry and sickness until you're old!

Steam Engine

— Zhen

Min'er's home is far from the town, so his family prepares their own food and drink.

Water is essential, but the water from the well is not very clean, and it's also far away, so boiling water is also done by themselves.

One day, a guest came to Min'er's house, so his father told him and his brother to boil water quickly.

Min'er and Cong'er took a kettle, filled it with rainwater, and placed it on a stove that burned all day long. After a while, the water boiled. A burst of steam lifted the kettle lid. So, they each poured a bowl of tea and went to give it to the guest and their father.

"Little brother, do you see anything special?" After they returned to the kitchen, Cong'er pointed to the kettle lid being lifted by the steam and asked Min'er.

"I don't know; please tell me."

"Watt, he was an Englishman. As a child, he was very attentive. Whenever he saw something or experienced something, he always asked himself, 'What is the principle behind this? Why is it done this way?' When he couldn't answer himself, he would ask his parents. One day, he was having lunch with his parents, and water was being boiled on the table. Before long, the water in the kettle was boiling. He saw the steam from the boiling water in the kettle lifting the lid, and he realized that the power of steam was very great. So, he devoted himself to studying year after year, and finally he invented this very important machine. Everyone in the world admires him. The saying 'Where there's a will, there's a way' is certainly true!"

"Brother, so he is the pioneer of the steam engine!"

"He can't be considered the first person. As early as the 2nd and 3rd centuries BC, Egyptians had already invented it, but it was simpler. Later, after the inventions and improvements of seven or eight European and American scientists, the greatest credit still goes to Watt. Even after he improved it, the steam engine didn't stop improving. The steam engine is still improving now."

"What is the structure of the steam engine?"

"The important components of a steam engine are six parts: the boiler, steam chest, steam valve, cylinder, piston, and flywheel. The water in the boiler turns into steam, which goes through the steam pipe to the steam chest. The steam valve controls the steam path and sends it to one end of the cylinder, pushing the piston and rotating the flywheel. When the steam valve is in the old position, steam goes from the left to the cylinder. When the steam valve is on the left, steam goes from the right to the cylinder. The piston moves back and forth, and the flywheel rotates continuously. Trains have this machine installed. We should call it a steam engine."

Crab

— Dazhai

Crabs are available in all seasons, so why are so many people eating them in "the ninth month for round crab roe and the tenth month for pointed crab roe"? Because at this time, the crabs are "full of brains and fat intestines," with that rich roe and delicious meat, arousing human saliva. Thus, they are coveted, tempted, and finally plundered and devoured.

From this, we can see that even with beautiful rivers and mountains, if there is no preservation of strength, there is no way to avoid being invaded. Not to mention other things, we only need to look at all of Africa, how all of it has become the territory of the great powers, and the indigenous people cannot be independent. This is a parallel.

The strong eat the weak, the law of natural selection. Crabs live in aquatic regions, do not compete with people, and do no harm to people. However, their meager pincers cannot defend their own safety. "It's hard for an old crab to escape a red back." They turn red, they are sacrificed. Don't blame the strong for being strong, only blame the weak for being weak!

Crabs turn red when cooked, which is very special. Of course, it has to do with the shell, but turtles also have shells. So, why don't turtles turn red when cooked? The reason is that although crabs are bluish-gray in color, they have various pigments such as blue, green, red, brown, and yellow, which are mixed under the skin. Among these pigments, red is the most durable, so after boiling, other pigments fall off, and only the red pigment remains. Shrimp are the same.

The Meaning of the Word "Mou" (某)

— Kangjianzhaifu

Probably all students in the third or fourth grade and above of elementary school know the word "mou" (某). And everyone knows how to use the word "mou". For example, "mou ren" (某人, someone), "mou chu" (某處, somewhere), this person "surnamed mou", "named mou". It generally represents an object that is not yet known.

In the era of autocracy, this word "mou" had several special uses. When officials spoke of the emperor's name, they could not read the name as it was, but could only use the word "mou" to replace it. Secondly, for the names of sages, such as Confucius's Kong Qiu, one could only read "Kong Mou", and Mencius's Meng Ke, one could only say "Meng Mou". It is said that this was to show respect, to avoid "offending the imperial majesty" or "desecrating the sacred".

Although the era of autocracy has passed, the word "mou" has become even more active in newspapers recently. Whenever elementary school students see newspapers, they misunderstand that the world now only has England, the United States, Russia, Italy, etc.,

The Work of Self-Governance

— (Zhang Muliang)

Zengzi said: "I examine myself three times a day: have I been disloyal in planning for others? Have I been untrustworthy in my interactions with friends? Have I not practiced what has been transmitted to me?" — The Analects

Explanation! Zengzi said, "I take three things to examine myself every day: First, when working for others, is there a place where I have not done my best? Second, in my interactions with friends, am I honest? Third, is there a problem that I have not carefully reviewed what the teacher has taught me?"

The World's Oldest Writing Tools

— You Mojun

Writing tools cannot escape paper, pen, and ink. In our country, in addition to the various inks used recently which are not unique to our country, the pen was made by Meng Tian of the Qin Dynasty, and the paper was made by Cai Lun of the Han Dynasty: everyone already knows this, so I won’t say more.

Speaking of paper, pens, and ink, people had already invented them four thousand years before Christ. Egypt is the world's oldest civilized country, and the ancient Egyptians were the most intelligent and creative people in the world. At that time, they made ink like this: mix a little plant gum juice in clear water, then scrape the soot from under the cooking pots and stir it into the gum water, and the ink is made. The pen? The manufacturing method is even simpler. Take a grass stem, sharpen one end, and you can dip it in ink to write.

Let’s talk about papermaking again. This is naturally not as simple as making pens and ink. Egypt has the Nile River, which is the water source for the entire country. A type of reed called Papyrus grows by the river. We now know that the fiber of plants can be used to make paper. However, the Egyptians already knew how to use “Papyrus” to make paper 4000 years BC. The method is to tear the "Papyrus" into thin strips, then press them flat, and then glue the thin strips together one by one. This creates sheets of white paper. The English word for paper is "Papel", which comes from Papyrus.

According to records, Meng Tian was born around 200 BC, and Cai Lun was born around 100 AD, so the invention of paper and pens in our country was really later compared to Egypt. This shows that the ancient Egyptians were the most intelligent and creative people in the world. There is also a hideous, intimidating, and overbearing "Mou Country" (某國), I don't know which country it is.

The troops of this "Mou Country" can arbitrarily conduct exercises and battles within our country, arbitrarily occupy railway stations, arbitrarily force people to sign and seal documents, and arbitrarily open fire and shoot. Aircraft can arbitrarily fly and reconnoiter in our country's airspace. The facts are all in front of us, but our newspapers still have to show respect to avoid "offending the imperial majesty."

Shuowen Jiezi says: "Mou, the ancient character for plum, a sour fruit." This "Mou" character really makes people feel sour when they look at it!

Types of Water

— Chu Yu

There are many types of water, and it has the greatest relationship with our bodies. From the perspective of electrolysis, there are distinctions between heavy water and light water, which means that within the elements of water, there are hydrogen isotopes with heavier specific gravity and lighter specific gravity. Ordinary water is a compound of two light hydrogen atoms and one oxygen atom, while heavy water is a compound of two heavy hydrogen atoms and one oxygen atom. Furthermore, considering the molecules of water, there is a difference between those formed by ordinary molecules, those composed of two molecules, and those composed of three molecules. The most suitable water for our bodies is a simple water with one molecule in addition to the composition of two or three molecules. If it is only one molecule of simple water, it is very (harmful to the body). Water with a single molecule is mostly transformed from water vapor. For example, rainwater falling from the sky is composed of a single molecule, but as it falls, it absorbs various gases and organic matter in the air, so that by the time it reaches the ground, it is almost the same as ordinary water. However, this water is actually not suitable for drinking. The worst type of water is distilled water, because it is water composed of an extremely simple molecule. Because it is too pure, after drinking this water, the osmotic action between the water quality and the cells in the body is too different, often leading to diarrhea. Most of the water we normally use is composed of more than two molecules, such as water from rivers, streams, and ponds. Water composed of three molecules is water that has melted from ice, which is why ice water is very beneficial to our bodies.

The Story of the White Mountain Crow (13)

— Xi

I looked up to the sky and cried out: "Is it only I who am not allowed to be happy? Let us leave this place, escape this cruel world. I will still seek my way out in the darkness, even if I am swallowed by some owl, to avoid seeing the happiness of others and causing me pain."

Thinking this, I set off again, flying aimlessly for a long time. When the first rays of dawn broke through, I saw the bell tower of the Saint Mary's Temple. In an instant, I had already flown there. Looking down, I saw that the garden below was ours. I flew down like lightning... Ah, the garden was empty!... I called out to my father and mother in vain... but there was no answering sound. The tree where my father usually perched, my mother's beloved bowl, were all gone. A sharp axe had already destroyed everything; I could no longer see the green lane where I grew up, only more than a hundred bundles of firewood.

(6)

I first searched for my father and mother in the garden, but all this was in vain; they must have taken refuge in some very distant place, and I could no longer get news of them. With a deep sense of melancholy, I went to stay on the ditch where my father had driven me away in the first place. I stayed there day and night, feeling endless sorrow. I could no longer sleep, nor could I eat anything; I seemed about to die of melancholy.

In this way, more than ten days passed in a row, and I just guarded this ditch, eagerly hoping for my parents to return. But knowing that one day after another passed, there was no hope at all. I thought to myself: they may be hiding in some very concealed place and cannot see me. If I raised my voice and uttered my special sound, then it would reach their ears, and after they heard it, they could not help but rush back to see their long-separated son. So I stretched out my neck and called out with all my might, calling out day and night, crying out again and again, "Father! Where are you? Do you still think of your unfortunate son? Mother! You loved me together, come back quickly! Meet me!"

Heaven! Please send a gust of wind to blow my weak voice far away, to blow it into the ears of my father and mother, so that they will immediately fly back and meet me!

Alas, I called out during the day and called out at night, until my throat was hoarse, but my father and mother never came back. How sad! How lonely! Seeing the parents and children in other crow nests reunited, loving each other, how envious I am!

Heaven! I can no longer guard this ditch. I must fly to the ends of the earth, fly to the corners of the world, fly all over the world, to find my father and mother! Goodbye! Friends! I am going! I am leaving from now on! (The End)
